B.   Tampering With Advertisements: It shall be unlawful to molest, remove,
injure, deface or destroy any lawful sign, signboard, show card, bill, poster
or advertisement of another. (1945 Code § 11-22)
5-3-8: THROWING MISSILES:
It shall be unlawful for any person to purposely or heedlessly cart or throw
any stone, dirt, refuse, or similar missiles into any public place, or at any
person or at, upon or against any buildings or premises of others without the
consent of the owner. (1945 Code § 11-21)
5-3-9: TRESPASSING:
A.   Unlawful To Commit Trespass: It shall be unlawful for any person, firm or
corporation to commit a trespass within the Village upon either public or
private property.
B.   Specific Trespasses: Without constituting any limitation upon the
provisions of subsection A of this section, any of the following acts by any
person, firm or corporation shall be deemed included among those that
constitute trespasses in violation of the provisions of said subsection A of
this section, and appropriate action may be taken hereunder at any time, or
from time to time, to prevent or suppress any violation or violations of this
section:
   1.   An entry upon the premises, or any part thereof, of another, including
any public property, in violation of a notice posted or exhibited at the main
entrance to said premises or at any point of approach or entry or in violation
of any notice, warning or protest given orally or in writing by any owner or
occupant thereof; or
   2.   The pursuit of a course of conduct or action incidental to the making
of an entry upon the land of another in violation of a notice posted or
exhibited at the main entrance to said premises or at any point of approach or
entry or in violation of any notice, warning or protest given orally or in
writing by any owner or occupant thereof; or
   3.   A failure or refusal to depart from the premises of another in the case
of being requested, either orally or in writing, to leave by any owner or
occupant thereof; or
   4.   An entry into or upon any vehicle, aircraft or watercraft made without
the consent of the person having the right to the possession or control
thereof, or a failure or refusal to leave any such vehicle, aircraft or
watercraft after being requested to leave by the person having such right.
(Ord., 10-1-1979)
C.   Penalty: Any person, firm or corporation violating any of the provisions
of this section shall, upon conviction thereof, be fined in an amount not
exceeding seven hundred fifty dollars ($750.00). (Ord., 10-1-1979; amd. 2017
Code)
5-3-10: WEAPONS CONTROL:
A.   Discharging Firearms: It shall be unlawful for any person to fire or
discharge, or cause to be fired or discharged, any firearm or gun within the
corporate limits of the Village, except any officer of the law who discharges a
firearm or gun in the performance of his or her official duties or by any
citizen who discharges a firearm or gun when lawfully defending his person or
property. (2017 Code)
B.   Concealed Weapons; Display In A Threatening Manner: It shall be unlawful
for any person not an officer duly authorized to carry the same to carry any
revolver, handgun, gun, firearm, pistol, dirk, dagger, dangerous knife, stun
gun, taser, billy club, metallic knuckles, or any knife, commonly referred to
as a switchblade knife, which has a blade that opens automatically by hand
pressure applied to a button, spring or other device in the handle of the
knife, or a ballistic knife, which is a device that propels a knifelike blade
as a projectile by means of a coil spring, elastic material, or compressed gas,
concealed on or about his person, or to flourish or display the same in a
threatening manner, except if carried or possessed in compliance with the
Firearm Concealed Carry Act, 430 Illinois Compiled Statutes 66/5, or the
unlawful use of weapons provisions contained in 720 Illinois Compiled Statutes
5/24-1. (1945 Code § 11-25; amd. 2017 Code)
5-3-11: HINDERING OR OBSTRUCTING VILLAGE OFFICIALS:
It shall be unlawful for any person to wilfully delay, hinder, resist or
obstruct any Village officer, or person authorized by him, in the discharge of
his duty; or to rescue, or attempt to rescue any person from the lawful custody
of said officer; or to neglect or refuse to obey any lawful order or direction
of such officer. (1945 Code § 11-19)
5-3-12: PENALTY:
Any person violating any provision of this chapter shall be subject to a fine
of not less than one hundred dollars ($100.00) nor more than seven hundred
fifty dollars ($750.00) for each offense. (1945 Code § 11-26; amd. 2017 Code)
CHAPTER 4
MINORS
SECTION:
5-4-1: Curfew Regulations
5-4-1: CURFEW REGULATIONS:
A.   Definitions: The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this
section, shall have the meanings ascribed to them in this subsection, except
where the context clearly indicates a different meaning:
   EMERGENCY: An unforeseen combination of circumstances or the resulting state
that calls for immediate action. The term "emergency" shall include, but is not
limited to, a fire, a natural disaster, an automobile accident, or any
situation requiring immediate action to prevent serious bodily injury or loss
of life.
   ESTABLISHMENT: Any privately owned place of business operated for a profit
to which the public is invited, including, but not limited to, any place of
amusement or entertainment.
   GUARDIAN:
   1.   A person who, under court order, is the guardian of the person of a
minor; or
   2.   A public or private agency with whom a minor has been placed by a
court.
   PARENT: A person who is:
   1.   A natural parent, adoptive parent, or stepparent of another person; or
   2.   At least eighteen (18) years of age and authorized by a parent or
guardian to have the care and custody of a minor.
   PUBLIC PLACE: Any place to which the public or a substantial group of the
public has access and includes, but is not limited to, streets, highways,
alleys, public ways, sidewalks, public property, and the common areas of
schools, hospitals, apartment houses, office buildings, transport facilities,
and shops.
   REMAIN: To:
   1.   Linger or stay; or
   2.   Fail to leave a public place or establishment when requested to do so
by a Police Officer or the owner, operator, Village official, or other person
in control of said public place or establishment.
   SERIOUS BODILY INJURY: Bodily injury that creates a substantial risk of
death or that causes death, serious permanent disfigurement, or protracted loss
or impairment of the function of any bodily member or organ.
B.   Prohibitions:
   1.   It shall be unlawful for any minor under the age of sixteen (16) to
remain or be present at or upon any public place or establishment at the
following times: From ten o'clock (10:00) P.M. on Monday to Sunday, inclusive,
and six o'clock (6:00) A.M. the following day.
   2.   No parent or guardian or other person shall knowingly permit a minor in
his or her custody or control to violate subsection B1 of this section.
C.   Exceptions: The restrictions contained in subsection B of this section
shall not apply to the following:
   1.   A minor accompanied by that minor's parent or guardian;
   2.   When a minor is on an errand at the direction of the minor's parent or
guardian, without any detour or stop;
   3.   When a minor is in a motor vehicle involved in interstate travel;
   4.   When a minor is engaged in an employment activity or going to or
returning home from an employment activity, without any detour or stop;
   5.   When a minor is on the sidewalk abutting the minor's place of residence
or abutting the residence of a next door neighbor if the neighbor did not
complain about the minor's presence;
   6.   When a minor is attending an official school, religious, or other
recreational activity supervised by adults and sponsored by a government or
governmental agency, a civic organization, or another similar entity that takes
responsibility for the minor, or going to or returning home from, without any
detour or stop, an official school, religious, or other recreational activity
sponsored by a government or governmental agency, a civic organization, or
another similar entity that takes responsibility for the minor;
   7.   When a minor is exercising First Amendment rights protected by the
United States Constitution, such as the free exercise of religion, freedom of
speech, and the right of assembly; or
   8.   When a minor is married or is an emancipated minor under the
Emancipation of Minors Act.
D.   Penalty: Any person who violates any provision of this section commits a
civil ordinance violation and shall, upon conviction, be fined not less than
one hundred dollars ($100.00) nor more than five hundred dollars ($500.00) for
each offense. (2017 Code)
CHAPTER 5
FIREWORKS AND EXPLOSIVES
SECTION:
5-5-1: Definitions
5-5-2: Prohibitions Generally
5-5-3: Storage Of Explosives
5-5-4: Consumer Fireworks And Pyrotechnic Displays
5-5-4-1: Permit Requirements
5-5-4-2: Site And Safety Requirements
5-5-4-3: Operator Qualifications And Restrictions
5-5-5: Enforcement
5-5-6: Violation; Penalties
5-5-1: DEFINITIONS:
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have
the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly
indicates a different meaning:
   CONSUMER FIREWORKS: Those fireworks that must comply with the construction,
chemical composition, and labeling regulations of the U.S. Consumer Products
Safety Commission, as set forth in 16 CFR parts 1500 and 1507, and classified
as fireworks UN0336 or UN0337 by the United States Department of Transportation
under 49 CFR 172.101. "Consumer fireworks" shall not include snake or glow worm
pellets; smoke devices; trick noisemakers known as party poppers, booby traps,
snappers, trick matches, cigarette loads, and auto burglar alarms; sparklers;
toy pistols, toy canes, toy guns or other devices in which paper or plastic
caps containing twenty five hundredths (0.25) grain or less of explosive
compound are used, provided they are so constructed that the hand cannot come
in contact with the cap when in place for the explosion; and toy pistol paper
or plastic caps that contain less than twenty hundredths (0.20) grain of
explosive mixture, the sale and use of which shall be permitted at all times.
   CONSUMER FIREWORKS DISPLAY: The detonation, ignition, or deflagration of
consumer fireworks to produce a visual or audible effect.
   CONSUMER FIREWORKS DISPLAY PERMIT: The permit issued by the President
authorizing the display of consumer fireworks within the corporate boundaries
of the Village of Dieterich.
   DISPLAY FIREWORKS: 1.3G or special effects fireworks or as further defined
in the Pyrotechnic Distributor and Operator Licensing Act, 225 Illinois
Compiled Statutes 227/1 et seq.
   FLAME EFFECT: The detonation, ignition, or deflagration of flammable gases,
liquids, or special materials to produce a thermal, physical, visual, or
audible effect before the public, invitees, or licensees, regardless of whether
admission is charged, in accordance with the National Fire Protection
Association 160 guidelines, and as may be further defined in the Pyrotechnic
Distributor and Operator Licensing Act, 225 Illinois Compiled Statutes 227/1 et
seq.
   LEAD PYROTECHNIC OPERATOR: An individual who is responsible for the safety,
setup, and discharges of the pyrotechnic display and who is licensed pursuant
to the Pyrotechnic Distributor and Operator Licensing Act, 225 Illinois
Compiled Statutes 227/1 et seq.
1.3G FIREWORKS: Those fireworks used for professional outdoor displays and
classified as fireworks under UN0333, UN0334, or UN0335 by the United States
Department of Transportation under 49 CFR 172.101.
   PERMITTEE: A person applying for a consumer fireworks display permit or
pyrotechnic display permit as provided herein.
   PERSON: Any individual, firm, partnership, limited partnership,
organization, corporation, limited liability company, company, consortium,
joint venture, commercial entity, association, proprietorship or other legal
entity, State, Municipality, or political subdivision of a State or any agency,
department, or instrumentality of the United States and any officer, agent,
member, or employee of these entities. The term shall also include an executor,
administrator, trustee, receiver or other representative appointed according to
law.
   PRESIDENT: The Village of Dieterich President, or his or her designee.
   PUBLIC USE: The use of property for recreational parks or schools purposes
by the general public.
   PYROTECHNIC DISPLAY: The detonation, ignition, or deflagration of display
fireworks or flame effects to produce visual or audible effects of an
exhibitional nature before the public, invitees, or licensees, regardless of
whether admission is charged, and as may be further defined in the Pyrotechnic
Distributor and Operator Licensing Act, 225 Illinois Compiled Statutes 227/1 et
seq.
   PYROTECHNIC DISPLAY PERMIT: The permit issued by the President authorizing
the display of display fireworks or flame effects within the corporate
boundaries of the Village of Dieterich.
   SPECIAL EFFECTS FIREWORKS: Pyrotechnic devices used for special effects by
professionals in the performing in conjunction with theatrical, musical, or
other productions that are similar to consumer fireworks in chemical
compositions and construction, but are not intended for consumer use and are
not labeled as such or identified as intended for indoor use. "Special effects
fireworks" are classified as fireworks UN0431 or UN0432 by the United States
Department of Transportation under 49 CFR 172.101. (Ord. 617-09, 6-1-2009; amd.
2017 Code)
5-5-2: PROHIBITIONS GENERALLY:
A.   Sale Of Fireworks: No person shall sell, expose for sale, offer for sale,
or display for sale consumer fireworks or display fireworks within the
corporate boundaries of the Village, except in compliance with the Pyrotechnic
Use Act, 425 Illinois Compiled Statutes 35/0.01 et seq., and the Fireworks
Regulation Act of Illinois, 425 Illinois Compiled Statutes 30/1 et seq. (Ord.
617-09, 6-1-2009; amd. 2017 Code)
B.   Display Of Fireworks:
   1.   It shall be unlawful to display, discharge, or give any consumer
fireworks display or pyrotechnic display within the corporate boundaries of the
Village, except in connection with public exhibitions as is provided in this
chapter. (Ord. 617-09, 6-1-2009)
   2.   It shall be unlawful to display, discharge, or give any consumer
fireworks display or pyrotechnic display on or over any property zoned R-1, R-
2, R-3, or R-4 within the corporate boundaries of the Village at any time,
except any property so zoned and actually used for public use as defined in
section
5-5-1 of this chapter. (Ord. 617-09, 6-1-2009; amd. 2017 Code)
5-5-3: STORAGE OF EXPLOSIVES:
All explosives including, but not limited to, consumer fireworks and display
fireworks, shall be stored or kept in accordance with the rules of the Illinois
State Fire Marshal, Federal and State regulations, this Code, and this chapter.
(Ord. 617-09, 6-1-2009)
5-5-4: CONSUMER FIREWORKS AND PYROTECHNIC DISPLAYS:
5-5-4-1: PERMIT REQUIREMENTS:
A.   Permits Required; Exemptions: No consumer fireworks display or pyrotechnic
display shall be given, displayed, discharged, and/or conducted unless a
consumer fireworks display permit or pyrotechnic display permit therefor is
first secured as provided in this section
5-5-4.
B.   Applications For Permits:
   1.   Consumer Fireworks Display Permit: Any person desiring to conduct a
consumer fireworks display within the corporate boundaries of the Village shall
first apply for a consumer fireworks display permit with the President by
filing the consumer fireworks display permit application, a true and accurate
copy of which is on file in the Village as Exhibit A and hereby incorporated by
reference as though fully stated.
   2.   Pyrotechnic Display Permit: Any person desiring to conduct a
pyrotechnic display within the corporate boundaries of the Village shall first
apply for a pyrotechnic display permit with the President by filing the
pyrotechnic display permit application, a true and accurate copy of which is on
file in the Village as Exhibit B and hereby incorporated by reference as though
fully stated.
C.   Bond, Insurance And State License Required: Any person desiring to conduct
a consumer fireworks display or pyrotechnic display within the corporate
boundaries of the Village shall be required to: 1) provide a one thousand
dollar ($1,000.00) public liability bond or cash bond with the Village in
connection with the consumer fireworks display permit application or
pyrotechnic display application; 2) provide proof of public liability insurance
in the amount of not less than one million dollars ($1,000,000.00), naming the
Village as an additional insured on a primary, noncontributory basis; and 3) be
properly licensed and/or trained by the Illinois State Fire Marshal as required
pursuant to the Pyrotechnic Use Act, 425 Illinois Compiled Statutes 35/0.01 et
seq.
D.   Permit Fee: Upon filing an application for a consumer fireworks display
permit or pyrotechnic display permit, the permittee shall pay to the Village a
nonrefundable fireworks display permit fee in the amount of one hundred fifty
dollars ($150.00).
E.   Investigation Of Applicant; Approval Or Denial Of Permits: The consumer
fireworks display permit application and/or pyrotechnic display permit
application shall be filed with the President not less than fifteen (15) days
before the date of the proposed consumer fireworks display or pyrotechnic
display unless agreed to otherwise by the Village and the President. The
President shall make, or cause to be made, an investigation of the site of the
proposed consumer fireworks display or pyrotechnic display for the purpose of
determining whether there is compliance with the provisions of this chapter.
The President shall confer with the Chief of the Dieterich Fire Protection
District for the purpose of inspecting the site of the proposed consumer
fireworks display or pyrotechnic display, determining the competence of the
actual operators of the consumer fireworks display or pyrotechnic display as
set forth in the consumer fireworks display permit application or pyrotechnic
display permit application, determining that the consumer fireworks display or
pyrotechnic display can be performed in full compliance with the rules adopted
by the Illinois State Fire Marshal, and determining that the consumer fireworks
display or pyrotechnic display shall not be hazardous to the property or
endanger any person or persons. No consumer fireworks display permit and/or
pyrotechnic display permit shall be issued unless it is signed by the Chief of
the Dieterich Fire Protection District. The President shall issue a consumer
fireworks display permit and/or pyrotechnic display permit if the applicant(s)
and the consumer fireworks display or pyrotechnic display comply with this
chapter and applicable Illinois and Federal law. The President shall have the
authority to deny any application for a consumer fireworks display permit or
pyrotechnic display permit if the applicant or the proposed consumer fireworks
display or pyrotechnic display site fails to comply with this chapter or
applicable State or Federal law.
F.   Nontransferability Of Permits: Consumer fireworks display permits and/or
pyrotechnic display permits shall not be transferable or assignable. The
attempted transfer or assignment of a consumer fireworks display permit or a
pyrotechnic display permit to any person shall terminate the consumer fireworks
display permit and/or pyrotechnic display permit.
G.   Possession Of Permits: The permittee shall have in his possession, at all
times while participating in a consumer fireworks display or pyrotechnic
display, a copy of the consumer fireworks display permit and/or pyrotechnic
display permit issued to him by the Village and shall show it to any person who
requests to see it. (Ord. 617-09, 6-1-2009; amd. 2017 Code)
5-5-4-2: SITE AND SAFETY REQUIREMENTS:
A.   Location Of Exhibition: A consumer fireworks display or pyrotechnic
display shall be permitted only when the actual point at which the consumer
fireworks, display fireworks, and/or flame effects are to be fired is at least
two hundred feet (200') from the nearest permanent building, public highway or
railroad or other means of travel, and one hundred feet (100') from the nearest
aboveground telephone line, electric line, tree or other overhead obstruction.
B.   Proximity Of Audiences: The audience at any consumer fireworks display or
pyrotechnic display shall be restrained behind lines of a perimeter at least
one hundred fifty feet (150') from the point at which the consumer fireworks,
display fireworks, and/or flame effects are discharged, and only persons
identified in the application shall be allowed inside said perimeter. (Ord.
617-09, 6-1-2009; amd. 2017 Code)
C.   Launching Projectiles; Falling Residue:
   1.   Launching Tubes: All launching tubes shall be set in the ground and/or
securely fastened to the ground, as approved by the President.
   2.   Angle Of Launch: All consumer fireworks, display fireworks, and/or
flame effects that fire a projectile shall be so set up so that the projectile
will go into the air as nearly as possible in a vertical direction; provided,
that where such consumer fireworks, display fireworks, and/or flame effects are
to be fired beside a lake or other large body of water, they may be directed in
such a manner that the falling residue from the detonation will fall into such
body of water. (Ord. 617-09, 6-1-2009)
D.   Wind: No consumer fireworks display or pyrotechnic display shall be held
during any windstorm in which the wind reaches a velocity of more than thirty
(30) miles per hour. In such cases, the President may authorize the consumer
fireworks display or pyrotechnic display at a future date suitable to the group
holding the consumer fireworks display or pyrotechnic display. (Ord. 617-09, 6-
1-2009; amd. 2017 Code)
E.   Fire Extinguishers Required: At least two (2) fire extinguishers approved
by the President shall be kept by the permittee at such locations designated by
the President.
F.   Transporting Fireworks And Flame Effects: All consumer fireworks, display
fireworks, and/or flame effects shall be transported and stored in a metal fire
resistant container with an automatic self-closing cover, as approved by the
President, and also complying with this chapter and applicable State and
Federal law. (Ord. 617-09, 6-1-2009)
G.   Disposal Of Undetonated Fireworks: Any consumer fireworks, display
fireworks, and/or flame effects that remain undetonated after the consumer
fireworks display or pyrotechnic display is concluded shall be immediately
disposed of outside of the corporate boundaries of the Village in accordance
with applicable law and in a safe manner. (Ord. 617-09, 6-1-2009; amd. 2017
Code)
5-5-4-3: OPERATOR QUALIFICATIONS AND RESTRICTIONS:
A.   Pyrotechnic Displays:
   1.   Lead Operators: The persons in actual charge of a pyrotechnic display
shall be able-bodied and at least twenty one (21) years of age and competent
for the task. Not less than two (2) licensed lead pyrotechnic operators shall
conduct and supervise each pyrotechnic display, and they shall be constantly on
duty during the pyrotechnic display. All operators shall be prohibited from
drinking alcoholic beverages or being under the influence of any controlled
substances at least five (5) hours immediately prior to and during the
pyrotechnic display.
   2.   Assistants: There shall be at all times not less than two (2) persons
assisting the licensed lead pyrotechnic operators on duty during a pyrotechnic
display. All persons assisting at a pyrotechnic display shall be prohibited
from drinking alcoholic beverages or being under the influence of any
controlled substances at least five (5) hours immediately prior to and during
the pyrotechnic display. Any person involved in and assisting in any function
related to the actual setup of a pyrotechnic display shall meet all of the
following minimum requirements:
      a.   Must be at least eighteen (18) years of age; and
      b.   Must be registered to assist a licensed lead pyrotechnics operator
with the Office of the Illinois State Fire Marshal; and
      c.   Has not been declared incompetent by any competent court by reason
of mental or physical defect or disease unless a court has since declared the
person competent; and
      d.   Has not wilfully violated any provision of the Pyrotechnic
Distributor and Operator Licensing Act, 225 Illinois Compiled Statutes 227/1 et
seq.; and
      e.   Does not have an addiction to or dependency on alcohol or drugs that
is likely to endanger the public at a pyrotechnic display; and
      f.   Has not been convicted in any jurisdiction of any felony within the
five (5) years prior to the pyrotechnic display; and
      g.   Must not be a fugitive from justice.
B.   Consumer Fireworks Displays: The persons in actual charge of a consumer
fireworks display shall be able-bodied and at least twenty one (21) years of
age and competent for the task. Each consumer fireworks display shall be
conducted and supervised by a consumer operator who has received training from
a consumer fireworks training class approved by the Office of the State Fire
Marshal, and he shall be constantly on duty during the consumer fireworks
display. There shall be at all times not less than one (1) person assisting the
consumer operator during a consumer fireworks display. All consumer operators
and any person involved and/or assisting in any function related to actual
setup and firing of a consumer fireworks display shall be prohibited from
drinking alcoholic beverages or being under the influence of any controlled
substances at least five (5) hours immediately prior to and during the consumer
fireworks display. Additionally, consumer operators and any person involved in
and assisting in any function related to the actual setup of a consumer
fireworks display shall meet all of the following minimum requirements:
   1.   Must be at least twenty one (21) years of age; and
   2.   Has not been declared incompetent by any competent court by reason of
mental or physical defect or disease unless a court has since declared the
person competent; and
   3.   Does not have an addiction to or dependency on alcohol or drugs that is
likely to endanger the public at a consumer fireworks display; and
   4.   Has not been convicted in any jurisdiction of any felony within the
five (5) years prior to the consumer fireworks display; and
   5.   Must not be a fugitive from justice. (Ord. 617-09, 6-1-2009; amd. 2017
Code)
5-5-5: ENFORCEMENT:
A.   Inspections: The President and the Chief of the Dieterich Fire Protection
District shall be authorized to inspect the location specified in the consumer
fireworks display permit application and/or pyrotechnic display permit
application as the site for the consumer fireworks display or pyrotechnic
display at any time, with or without notice to the permittee. In the event the
President determines that a violation of this chapter and/or State or Federal
law has occurred, the President shall:
   1.   Notify the Dieterich Fire Protection District; and
   2.   Order the permittee to cease the consumer fireworks display or
pyrotechnic display; and
   3.   Immediately revoke the permittee's consumer fireworks display permit
and/or pyrotechnic display permit; and
   4.   Take necessary steps to close the site specified in the consumer
fireworks display permit application and/or pyrotechnic display permit
application as the site for the consumer fireworks display or pyrotechnic
display and otherwise prevent the permittee continuing or giving a consumer
fireworks display or pyrotechnic display within the corporate boundaries of the
Village; and
   5.   Direct the Village, via the Office of the Village Attorney, to issue
appropriate citations to the permittee or such person violating this chapter,
or take such other action as authorized by applicable law, including, but not
limited to, the arrest of the permittee or such person violating this chapter;
and (Ord. 617-09, 6-1-2009; amd. 2017 Code)
   6.   Take possession of any undetonated consumer fireworks, display
fireworks, and/or flame effects, and safely store the same pending an order of
a court of competent jurisdiction.
B.   Agreement With Fire Protection District: The President is hereby
authorized to execute such documents as may be necessary to enter into
agreements with the Dieterich Fire Protection District to perform such
inspection and enforcement services as required under this chapter and is
authorized to reimburse the Dieterich Fire Protection District for said
services in an amount not to exceed the amount of the permit fee referenced in
subsection
 5-5-4-1D of this chapter. (Ord. 617-09, 6-1-2009)
5-5-6: VIOLATION; PENALTIES:
In addition to any remedy or penalty provided in 425 Illinois Compiled Statutes
35/1 et seq., any person who violates any provision of this chapter commits a
civil ordinance violation. The Village Attorney shall prosecute such violation.
Upon entry of a judgment in favor of the Village, the violator(s) shall be
fined not less than five hundred dollars ($500.00) and not more than seven
hundred fifty dollars ($750.00) for each violation. Each day that a violation
of this chapter continues shall constitute a separate and distinct violation
for which the violator(s) shall be fined. In addition to any fine, the Village
may seek injunctive and declaratory relief directing the violator(s) to cure or
abate the violation. (Ord. 617-09, 6-1-2009)
CHAPTER 6
DISCRIMINATION IN HOUSING
SECTION:
5-6-1: Village Policy
5-6-2: Definitions
5-6-3: Prohibited Acts
5-6-4: Penalty
5-6-1: VILLAGE POLICY:
A.   In furthering the policy of the State of Illinois as expressed in its
Constitution and other laws and in order that the safety and general welfare,
peace and health of all the inhabitants of the Village may be ensured, it is
hereby declared the policy of the Village to assure equal opportunity to all
residents, regardless of race, color, religion, gender, creed, ancestry,
national origin, or physical or mental disability, order of protection status,
familial status, marital status, age, military status, sexual orientation,
pregnancy or unfavorable discharge from the military to live in decent,
sanitary, healthful, standard living quarters.
B.   It is the policy of the Village that no owner, lessee, sublessee,
assignee, managing agent, or other person, firm or corporation having the right
to sell, rent, lease or otherwise control any housing accommodation and/or real
property within the Village, or any agent of these, shall refuse to sell, rent,
lease, or otherwise deny to or withhold from any person or group of persons
such housing accommodations and/or real property because of race, color,
religion, gender, creed, ancestry, national origin, or physical or mental
disability, order of protection status, familial status, marital status, age,
military status, sexual orientation, pregnancy or unfavorable discharge from
the military of such person or persons or discriminate against any person or
persons because of race, color, religion, gender, creed, ancestry, national
origin, or physical or mental disability, order of protection status, familial
status, marital status, age, military status, sexual orientation, pregnancy or
unfavorable discharge from the military in the conditions, terms, privileges of
the sale, rental or lease of any housing accommodation and/or property or in
the furnishing of facilities and/or services in connection therewith. (Ord.
612-09, 3-2-2009; amd. 2017 Code)
C.   Relocation shall be carried out in a manner that will promote maximum
choice within the community's total housing supply; lessen racial, ethnic, and
economic concentrations; and facilitate desegregation and racially inclusive
patterns of occupancy and use of public and private facilities. (Ord. 612-09,
3-2-2009)
5-6-2: DEFINITIONS:
Unless a different meaning clearly appears from the context, the following
terms shall have the meanings as described in this section and as used in this
chapter:
   DECENT, SANITARY, HEALTHFUL, STANDARD LIVING QUARTERS: Housing which is in a
sound, clean, and weathertight condition in conformance with applicable local,
State and national codes.
   DISCRIMINATE; DISCRIMINATION: Any difference expressed in any way toward a
person or persons in the terms of the sale, exchange, lease, rental or
financing for housing accommodation and/or real property in regard to such
sale, exchange, rental, lease or finance because of race, color, religion,
gender, creed, ancestry, national origin, or physical or mental disability,
order of protection status, familial status, marital status, age, military
status, sexual orientation, pregnancy or unfavorable discharge from the
military of such person.
   FINANCIAL INSTITUTION: Any person, institution or business entity of any
kind which loans money to persons and receives as security for said loans a
secured interest of any kind in the real property of the borrower.
   HOUSING ACCOMMODATION: Any building, structure, or portion thereof which is
used or occupied, or maintained, arranged or designed to be used or occupied,
as a home, residence or sleeping place of one (1) or more human beings, or any
real estate so used, designated or intended for such use.
   OWNER: Any person/persons who hold legal or equitable title to or own any
beneficial interest in any real property or who hold legal or equitable title
to shares of, or hold any beneficial interest in, any real estate cooperative
which owns any real property and/or housing accommodations.
   REAL ESTATE BROKER: Any person, partnership, association, corporation and/or
agent thereof who, for a fee or other valuable consideration, offers, sells,
purchases, exchanges or rents, or negotiates for the sale, purchase, exchange
or rental of, a housing accommodation and/or real property of another, or
collects rental for the use of housing accommodation and/or real property of
another.
   REAL PROPERTY: Any real estate, vacant land, building, structure or housing
accommodations within the corporate limits of the Village of Dieterich,
Illinois. (Ord. 612-09, 3-2-2009; amd. 2017 Code)
5-6-3: PROHIBITED ACTS:
It shall be unlawful for any owner of real estate, lessee, sublessee, real
estate broker or salesman, financial institution or employee of the financial
institution, advertiser, or agent of any or all of the foregoing, to
discriminate against any person or persons because of their race, color,
religion, gender, creed, ancestry, national origin, or physical or mental
disability, order of protection status, familial status, marital status, age,
military status, sexual orientation, pregnancy or unfavorable discharge from
the military with regard to the sale, exchange or rental or any dealing
concerning any housing accommodation and/or real property. In addition to the
foregoing, it shall also be unlawful for any real estate broker or employee
thereof, owner or other person, or financial institution dealing with housing
or real property in the Village:
A.   To discriminate against any person in the availability of or the price,
terms, conditions, or privileges of any kind relating to the sale, rental,
lease, or occupancy of any housing accommodation or real property in the
Village or in furnishing of any facilities or services in connection therewith.
B.   To publish or circulate, or cause to be published or circulated, any
notice, statement or advertisement, or to announce a policy, or to use any form
of application for the purchase, lease, rental or financing of real property,
or to make any record of inquiry in connection with the prospective purchase,
rental or lease of such real estate which expresses directly or indirectly any
discrimination as to race, color, religion, gender, creed, ancestry, national
origin, or physical or mental disability, order of protection status, familial
status, marital status, age, military status, sexual orientation, pregnancy or
unfavorable discharge from the military of any person.
C.   To discriminate in connection with lending money, guaranteeing loans,
accepting mortgages or otherwise obtaining or making available funds for the
purchase, acquisition, construction, rehabilitation, repair or maintenance of
any housing accommodation and/or real property.
D.   To solicit for sale or lease, or listing for the sale or lease, of any
housing accommodation and/or real property on the grounds of loss of value
because of the present or prospective entry into any neighborhood of any person
or persons of any particular race, color, religion, gender, creed, ancestry,
national origin, or physical or mental disability, order of protection status,
familial status, marital status, age, military status, sexual orientation,
pregnancy or unfavorable discharge from the military.
E.   To distribute or cause to be distributed written material or statements
designed to induce any owner of any housing accommodation and/or real property
to sell or lease his or her property because of any present or prospective
change in the race, color, religion, gender, creed, ancestry, national origin,
or physical or mental disability, order of protection status, familial status,
marital status, age, military status, sexual orientation, pregnancy or
unfavorable discharge from the military of persons in the neighborhood.
F.   To make any misrepresentation concerning the listing for sale, or the
anticipated listing for sale, or the sale of any housing accommodation and/or
real property for the purpose of inducing or attempting to induce the sale or
listing for sale of any housing accommodation and/or real property by
representing that the presence or anticipated presence of persons of any
particular race, color, religion, gender, creed, ancestry, national origin, or
physical or mental disability, order of protection status, familial status,
marital status, age, military status, sexual orientation, pregnancy or
unfavorable discharge from the military in the area will or may result in the
lowering of property values in the block, neighborhood or area in which the
property is located.
G.   For an owner to solicit any real estate broker to sell, rent or otherwise
deal with such owner's housing accommodations and/or real property with any
limitation on its sale based on race, color, religion, gender, creed, ancestry,
national origin, or physical or mental disability, order of protection status,
familial status, marital status, age, military status, sexual orientation,
pregnancy or unfavorable discharge from the military.
H.   For an owner to refuse to sell, rent, or otherwise deal with any housing
accommodation and/or real property because of race, color, religion, gender,
creed, ancestry, national origin, or physical or mental disability, order of
protection status, familial status, marital status, age, military status,
sexual orientation, pregnancy or unfavorable discharge from the military of the
proposed buyer or tenant. (Ord. 612-09, 3-2-2009; amd. 2017 Code)
5-6-4: PENALTY:
Any person convicted of violating any of the provisions of this chapter shall
be punishable by a fine of not less than one hundred dollars ($100.00) nor more
than seven hundred fifty dollars ($750.00). Each day a violation continues
shall constitute a separate violation. This section shall in no way abrogate or
impair the right of the Village to specifically enforce, by any legal means,
any of the provisions of this chapter. (Ord. 612-09, 3-2-2009; amd. 2017 Code)
CHAPTER 7
NOISE CONTROL
SECTION:
5-7-1: Purpose
5-7-2: Definitions
5-7-3: General Prohibition
5-7-4: Noises Prohibited
5-7-5: Exemptions
5-7-6: Penalty
5-7-1: PURPOSE:
The purpose of this chapter is to protect, preserve, and promote the health,
safety, welfare, peace, and quiet of the citizens of the Village of Dieterich,
Illinois, through the reduction, control, and prevention of loud and raucous
noise, or any noise which unreasonably disturbs, injures, or endangers the
comfort, repose, health, peace, or safety of reasonable persons of ordinary
sensitivity. (Ord. 897-18, 5-21-2018)
5-7-2: DEFINITIONS:
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have
the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly
indicates a different meaning:
   EMERGENCY: Shall mean any occurrence or set of circumstances involving
actual or imminent physical trauma or property damage demanding immediate
attention.
   EMERGENCY WORK: Shall mean any work performed for the purpose of preventing
or alleviating physical trauma or property damage, whether actually caused or
threatened by an emergency, or work or private or public utilities when
restoring utility service.
   NOISE SENSITIVE AREA: Shall mean any area, which includes a posted area
where a school, hospital, nursing home, church, court, public library, or
similar institution is located.
   PERSON: Shall mean any individual, firm, corporation, limited liability
company, partnership, society, association or other legal entity, any public or
private institution, the State of Illinois, municipal corporation or political
subdivision of the State, or any other business unit.
   PUBLIC RIGHT-OF-WAY: Shall mean any street, avenue, boulevard, highway,
sidewalk, alley, or similar place normally accessible to the public which is
owned or controlled by a government entity.
   PUBLIC SPACE: Shall mean any real property or structures on real property
owned by a government entity and normally accessible to the public, including
but not limited to parks and other recreational areas.
   RESIDENTIAL AREA: Shall mean any real property which contains a structure or
building in which one or more persons reside, provided that the structure or
building is properly zoned, or is legally nonconforming, for residential use in
accordance with the terms and maps of the Village of Dieterich, Illinois,
zoning ordinance no. 487, as amended from time to time.
   VILLAGE: Shall mean the Village of Dieterich, Illinois. (Ord. 897-18, 5-21-
2018)
5-7-3: GENERAL PROHIBITION:
A.   No person shall make, continue or cause to be made or continued, the
following activities:
   1.   Any unreasonably loud or raucous noise; or
   2.   Any noise which disturbs, injures, or endangers the comfort, repose,
health, peace, or safety of reasonable persons of ordinary sensitivity within
the jurisdictional limits of the Village.
B.   Factors in determining whether a sound is unreasonably loud or raucous
include, but are not limited to, the following:
   1.   The proximity of the sound to sleeping facilities, whether residential
or commercial;
   2.   The land use, nature, and zoning of both the area from which the sound
emanates and the area where the sound is received or perceived;
   3.   The time the sound occurs;
   4.   The duration of the sound; and,
   5.   Whether the sound is recurrent, intermittent, or constant. (Ord. 897-
18, 5-21-2018)
5-7-4: NOISES PROHIBITED:
The following acts are declared to be per se violations of this chapter. This
enumeration does not constitute an exclusive list:
A.   Unreasonable Noises: The unreasonable making of, or knowingly and
unreasonably permitting to be made, any unreasonably loud, boisterous or
unusual noise, disturbance, commotion or vibration in any boarding facility,
dwelling, place of business or other structure, or upon any public street,
park, or other place or building. The ordinary and usual sounds, noises,
commotion or vibration incidental to the operation of these places when
conducted in accordance with the usual standards of practice and in a manner
which will not unreasonably disturb the peace and comfort of adjacent
residences or which will not detrimentally affect the operators of adjacent
places of business are exempted from this provision.
B.   Vehicle Horns, Signaling Devices, And Similar Devices: The sounding of any
horn, signaling device, or other similar device on any automobile, motorcycle,
or other vehicle on any right-of- way or in any public space of the Village for
more than ten (10) consecutive seconds. The sounding of any horn, signaling
device, or other similar device as a danger warning is exempt from this
prohibition.
C.   Nonemergency Signaling Devices: Sounding or permitting the sounding of any
amplified signal from any bell, chime, siren, whistle or similar device,
intended primarily for nonemergency purposes, from any place for more than ten
(10) consecutive seconds in an hourly period. The reasonable sounding of such
devices by houses of religious worship, ice cream trucks, and seasonal
contribution solicitors or by the Village for traffic control purposes are
exempt from the operation of this provision.
D.   Emergency Signaling Devices: The intentional sounding or permitting the
sounding outdoors of any emergency signaling device including fire, burglar,
civil defense alarm, siren, whistle, or similar emergency signaling device,
except in an emergency or except as provided in subsections D1 and D2 of this
section:
   1.   Testing of an emergency signaling device shall occur between seven
o'clock (7:00) A.M. and seven o'clock (7:00) P.M. Any testing shall use the
minimum cycle test time. In no case shall such test time exceed five (5)
minutes. Testing of the emergency signaling system shall not occur more than
once in each calendar month; or,
   2.   Sounding or permitting the sounding of any exterior burglar or fire
alarm or any motor vehicle burglar alarm shall terminate within fifteen (15)
minutes of activation unless an emergency exists. If a false or accidental
activation of an alarm occurs more than twice in a calendar month, the owner or
a person responsible for the alarm shall be in violation of this chapter.
E.   Radios, Televisions, Boom Boxes, Phonographs, Stereos, Musical Instruments
And Similar Devices:
   1.   The use or operation of a radio, televisions, boom boxes, phonographs,
stereos, musical instruments or similar device that produces or reproduces
sound in a manner that is plainly audible to any person other than the player
(s) or operator(s) of the device, and those who are voluntarily listening to
the sound, and which unreasonably disturbs the peace, quiet, and comfort of
neighbors and passersby, or is plainly audible at a distance of fifty feet
(50') from any person in a commercial, industrial area, or public space.
   2.   The use or operation of a radio, televisions, boom boxes, phonographs,
stereos, musical instruments or similar device that produces or reproduces
sound in a manner that is plainly audible to any person other than the player
(s) or operator(s) of the device, and those who are voluntarily listening to
the sound, and unreasonably disturbs the peace, quiet and comfort of neighbors
in residential area or noise-sensitive area, including multifamily or single-
family dwellings.
F.   Loudspeakers, Amplifiers, Public Address Systems, And Similar Devices:
   1.   The unreasonably loud and raucous use or operation of a loudspeaker,
amplifier, public address system, or other device for producing or reproducing
sound between the hours of ten o'clock (10:00) P.M. and seven o'clock (7:00)
A.M. on weekdays, and ten o'clock (10:00) P.M. and ten o'clock (10:00) A.M. on
weekends and holidays in the following areas:
      a.   Within or adjacent to residential area or noise sensitive area;
      b.   Within public space if the sound is plainly audible across the real
property line of the public space from which the sound emanates, and is
unreasonably loud and raucous.
   2.   This shall not apply to any public performance, gathering, or parade
for which prior permission has been obtained from the Village.
G.   Yelling, Shouting, And Similar Activities: Yelling, shouting, hooting,
whistling, or singing in residential area or noise sensitive area or in public
places, between the hours of ten o'clock (10:00) P.M. and seven o'clock (7:00)
A.M., or at any time or place so as to unreasonably disturb the quiet, comfort,
or repose of reasonable persons of ordinary sensitivities.
H.   Animals And Birds: Unreasonably loud and raucous noise emitted by an
animal or bird for which a person is responsible. A person is responsible for
an animal if the person owns, controls or otherwise cares for the animal or
bird. Sounds made by animals or birds in animal shelters, kennels, veterinary
hospitals, pet shops or pet kennels licensed under and in compliance with
licensing and permitting provisions set forth in this Code are exempt from this
subsection H.
I.   Loading Or Unloading Merchandise, Materials, Equipment: The creation of
unreasonably loud, raucous, and excessive noise in connection with the loading
or unloading of any vehicle at a place of business or residence.
J.   Construction Or Repair Of Buildings, Excavations Of Streets And Highways:
The construction, demolition, alteration or repair of any building or the
excavation of streets and highways other than between the hours of seven
o'clock (7:00) A.M. and seven o'clock (7:00) P.M., on Monday through Friday,
and eight o'clock (8:00) A.M. and six o'clock (6:00) P.M. on Saturdays. In
cases of emergency, construction or repair noises are exempt from this
provision. In nonemergency situations, the Village Clerk, or his/her designee,
may grant permission, upon written request, if the Village Clerk, or his/her
designee, determines that the public health and safety, as affected by loud and
raucous noise caused by construction or repair of buildings or excavation of
streets and highways between the hours of seven o'clock (7:00) P.M. and seven
o'clock (7:00) A.M., will not be impaired, and if the Village Clerk, or his/her
designee, further determine that loss or inconvenience would result to a party
of interest. The permission in nonemergency cases shall be valid for a period
of not more than three (3) days. The permission may be renewed once for a
period of three (3) days or less.
K.   Noise Sensitive Areas (Schools, Courts, Churches, Hospitals, And Similar
Institutions): The creation of any unreasonably loud and raucous noise adjacent
to any noise-sensitive area while it is in use, which unreasonably interferes
with the workings of the institution or which disturbs the persons in these
institutions, provided that conspicuous signs delineating the boundaries of the
noise-sensitive area are displayed in the streets surrounding the noise-
sensitive area.
L.   Grounds Maintenance Equipment, Blowers, And Similar Devices: In
residential area or noise sensitive areas between the hours of nine o'clock (9:
00) P.M. and seven o'clock (7:00) A.M., the operation of any noise-creating
blower, power fan, or any internal combustion engine, including, but not
limited to power- driven lawn or garden maintenance equipment, the operation of
which causes noise due to the explosion of operating gases or fluids, provided
that the noise is unreasonably loud and raucous and can be heard across the
property line of the property from which it emanates.
M.   Commercial Establishments Adjacent To Residential Property: Unreasonably
loud and raucous noise from the premises of any commercial establishment,
including any outdoor area which is part of or under the control of the
establishment, between the hours of eleven o'clock (11:00) P.M. and seven
o'clock (7:00) A.M. which is plainly audible at a distance of five feet (5')
from any residential property.
N.   Amplified Music And Sound Systems; Live Or Recorded Performances:
Amplified music and sound systems of any type or any type of live or recorded
performance.
O.   Sound-Amplifying Device Within A Multiple-Family Structure: It shall be
unlawful to use or operate a sound-amplifying device so that the device
produces loud and raucous sounds within a multiple-family structure from eleven
o'clock (11:00) P.M. to ten o'clock (10:00) A.M., local time, Sunday through
Saturday. (Ord. 897-18, 5-21-2018)
5-7-5: EXEMPTIONS:
The prohibitions set out in sections
5-7-3 and
 5-7-4 of this chapter, shall not apply to, in addition to the exemptions
specifically set forth within section
 5-7-4 of this chapter, the sounds caused by the following:
A.   Motor vehicles on traffic ways of the Village, provided that the
prohibition of subsection
5-7-4B of this chapter continues to apply.
B.   Repairs of utility structures which pose a clear and immediate danger to
life, health, or significant loss of property.
C.   Sirens, whistles, or bells lawfully used by emergency vehicles, or other
alarm systems used in case of fire, collision, civil defense, police activity,
or imminent danger, provided that the prohibition contained in subsection
5-7-4D of this chapter continues to apply.
D.   The emission of sound for the purpose of alerting persons to the existence
of an emergency or the emission of sound in the performance of emergency work.
E.   Repairs or excavations of bridges, streets or highways by or on behalf of
the Village, the State, or the Federal government, between the hours of seven
o'clock (7:00) P.M. and seven o'clock (7:00) A.M., when public welfare and
convenience renders it impractical to perform the work between seven o'clock
(7:00) A.M. and seven o'clock (7:00) P.M.
F.   Outdoor school and playground activities. Reasonable activities conducted
on public playgrounds and public or private school grounds, which are conducted
in accordance with the manner in which such spaces are generally used,
including but not limited to school athletic and school entertainment events.
G.   Other outdoor events. Authorized sporting events, community events, or
other similar outdoor events. (Ord. 897-18, 5-21-2018)
5-7-6: PENALTY:
Any person who violates any provision of this chapter commits a civil ordinance
violation and shall, upon conviction, be fined not less than one hundred
dollars ($100.00), nor more than five hundred dollars ($500.00), for each
offense. Each day a violation of this chapter is allowed to continue shall
constitute a separate offense. (Ord. 897-18, 5-21-2018)
TITLE 6
MOTOR VEHICLES AND TRAFFIC
CHAPTER 1
GENERAL TRAFFIC PROVISIONS
SECTION:
6-1-1: Definitions
6-1-2: Authority To Direct Traffic
6-1-1: DEFINITIONS:
As used in this title, the terms "streets" and "streets and alleys" include
streets, alleys, sidewalks, and any public drives or ways open to public use.
(1945 Code §16-14; amd. 2017 Code)
6-1-2: AUTHORITY TO DIRECT TRAFFIC:
In the event of fire, storm, public emergency or unusual crowded traffic
conditions, any Village officer is empowered to direct traffic or halt traffic
or close streets to traffic when apparently necessary for safety, and all
persons shall heed and obey the directions of any such officer. Any person
violating this section shall be subject to a fine of not less than two hundred
fifty dollars ($250.00) nor more than seven hundred fifty dollars ($750.00).
(1945 Code §16-15; amd. 2017 Code)
CHAPTER 2
PARKING REGULATIONS
SECTION:
6-2-1: Parking To Obstruct Traffic Prohibited
6-2-2: Parking Prohibited In Specified Places
6-2-3: Truck Parking In Residential Districts
6-2-1: PARKING TO OBSTRUCT TRAFFIC PROHIBITED:
No automobile, truck, trailer, camper or other vehicle shall be so parked or
placed at any place within the Village in such manner or position as to
obstruct the free use of any street, alley, sidewalk or driveway, or in such
manner that it unnecessarily extends into any street, alley or driveway. Any
person violating this section shall be subject to a fine of not less than ten
dollars ($10.00) nor more than one hundred dollars ($100.00). (1945 Code §16-
13; amd. 2017 Code)
6-2-2: PARKING PROHIBITED IN SPECIFIED PLACES:
A.   Except when necessary to avoid conflict with other traffic, or in
compliance with law or the directions of a Police Officer or official traffic
control device, no person shall:
   1.   Stop, stand or park a vehicle:
      a.   On the roadway side of any vehicle stopped or parked at the edge or
curb of a street.
      b.   On a sidewalk.
      c.   Within an intersection.
      d.   On a crosswalk.
      e.   Between a safety zone and the adjacent curb or within thirty feet
(30') of points on the curb immediately opposite the ends of a safety zone,
unless a different length is indicated by signs or markings.
      f.   Alongside or opposite any street excavation or obstruction when
stopping, standing or parking would obstruct traffic.
      g.   Upon any bridge or other elevated structure upon a highway or within
a highway tunnel.
      h.   On any railroad tracks. A violation of this subsection shall result
in a mandatory fine of five hundred dollars ($500.00) or fifty (50) hours of
community service.
      i.   On any controlled access highway.
      j.   In the area between roadways of a divided highway, including
crossovers.
      k.   In a public parking area if the vehicle does not display a current
annual registration sticker or current temporary permit pending registration.
      l.   At any place where official signs prohibit stopping.
   2.   Stand or park a vehicle, whether occupied or not, except momentarily to
pick up or discharge passengers:
      a.   In front of a public or private driveway.
      b.   Within fifteen feet (15') of a fire hydrant.
      c.   Within twenty feet (20') of a crosswalk at an intersection.
      d.   Within thirty feet (30') upon the approach to any flashing signal,
stop sign, yield sign, or traffic control signal located at the side of a
roadway.
      e.   Within twenty feet (20') of the driveway entrance to any Fire
Station and on the side of a street opposite the entrance to any Fire Station
within seventy five feet (75') of such entrance (when properly sign-posted).
      f.   At any place where official signs prohibit standing.
   3.   Park a vehicle, whether occupied or not, except temporarily for the
purpose of and while actually engaged in loading or unloading property or
passengers:
      a.   Within fifty feet (50') of the nearest rail of a railroad crossing.
      b.   At any place where official signs prohibit parking.
B.   No person shall move a vehicle not lawfully under his control into any
such prohibited area or away from a curb such distance as is unlawful.
C.   Any person violating any provision of this section shall be subject to a
fine of not less than two hundred fifty dollars ($250.00) nor more than seven
hundred fifty dollars ($750.00). (1945 Code § 16-13; amd. 2017 Code)
6-2-3: TRUCK PARKING IN RESIDENTIAL DISTRICTS:
No person operating a motor vehicle in excess of twelve thousand (12,000)
pounds or with more than six (6) tires in contact with the ground or road
surface shall stand or park such vehicle upon any street where the primary use
of the structures fronting upon said street is for residential purposes, except
for the purpose of making a delivery or pick up of merchandise or material, in
which event, such standing or parking shall be permitted for a period not to
exceed one (1) hour; provided, however, that trucks engaged in the transporting
of household possessions of persons moving into or out of a dwelling unit shall
be permitted to park or stand said truck in front of the residence of a person
so moving for a period not to exceed the duration of moving said possessions.
Anyone in violation of this section shall be fined two hundred fifty dollars
($250.00) for the first offense and seven hundred fifty dollars ($750.00) for
each offense thereafter. Each day a violation of this section continues shall
be considered a separate offense. (Ord. 589-08, 4-7-2008; amd. 2017 Code)
CHAPTER 3
TRAFFIC SCHEDULES
SECTION:
6-3-1: Traffic Schedules Adopted
6-3-1: TRAFFIC SCHEDULES ADOPTED:
Unless otherwise provided in this title, the ordinances of the Village
establishing driving restrictions and prohibitions on specific streets in the
Village are hereby adopted by reference as if set out at length herein. Copies
of said ordinances are on file in the Office of the Village Clerk for public
use and inspection. (2017 Code)
CHAPTER 4
NON-HIGHWAY VEHICLES
SECTION:
6-4-1: Definitions
6-4-2: Operation On Streets And Alleys
6-4-3: Permitted Crossing
6-4-4: Required Equipment
6-4-5: Lights
6-4-6: Required Seating; Passengers
6-4-7: Age Of Operator, License
6-4-8: Speed Limit
6-4-9: Ordinance And Vehicle Code Obeyance
6-4-10: Village License; Annual Fee
6-4-11: Mandatory Insurance
6-4-12: Release Of Liability
6-4-13: License Revocation
6-4-14: Violations; Punishment
6-4-1:    DEFINITIONS:
The following words, terms and phrases, when used in this chapter, shall have
the meanings ascribed to them in this section, except where the context clearly
indicates a different meaning.
 
NON-HIGHWAY VEHICLE: Shall mean a motor vehicle not specifically designed to be
                     used on a public highway, including:
                     A. An All-Terrain Vehicle, as that term is defined in
                    section 1-101.8 of the Illinois Vehicle Code, provided,
                     however, that this shall not include what is commonly
                     known as three-wheelers or four-wheelers;
                    B. A Golf Cart, as that term is defined in section 1-123.9
                     of the Illinois Vehicle Code; or,
                    C. A Recreational Off-Highway Vehicle, as that term is
                     defined in section 1-168.8 of the Illinois Vehicle Code.
 
Anything contained in this chapter to the contrary notwithstanding, for
purposes of this chapter, the term "Non-Highway Vehicle" shall not include an
Off-Highway Motorcycle, as that term is defined in section 1-153.1 of the
Illinois Vehicle Code. (Ord. 914-2018, 9-5-2018; amd. Ord. 935-2019, 2-18-2019;
Ord. 977-2019, 9-23-2019)
6-4-2:    OPERATION ON STREETS AND ALLEYS:
A.   Non-highway vehicles may be operated on those streets and alleys under the
jurisdiction and control of the Village of Dieterich, Illinois, where the
posted speed limit is thirty five (35) miles per hour or less, subject to the
requirements and regulations of this chapter.
B.   Except as provided in section
 6-4-3 of this chapter, it shall be unlawful to operate a non-highway vehicle
on:
   1.   Illinois Route 33; and,
   2.   Main Street.
C.   Non-highway vehicles shall be operated in the same direction as traffic.
D.   It shall be unlawful to operate a non-highway vehicle on any sidewalks or
other locations within the corporate limits of the Village of Dieterich,
Illinois, except as permitted by this chapter. (Ord. 914-2018, 9-5-2018)
6-4-3: PERMITTED CROSSING:
A.   Non-highway vehicles shall be permitted to make a direct crossing on U.S.
Route 33 (Center Street), but only while traveling on either Pine Street or
Loda Street; and,
B.   Non-highway vehicles shall be permitted to make a direct crossing on Main
Street, but only while traveling on Elm Street or Church Street. (Ord. 935-
2019, 2-18-2019)
December 2019
6-4-4: REQUIRED EQUIPMENT:
No non-highway vehicle shall be operated on any street or roadway under the
jurisdiction and control of the Village of Dieterich, Illinois, unless non-
highway vehicle is equipped with the following equipment, which must be kept in
good working condition at all times:
A.   Brakes;
B.   Steering apparatus;
C.   Tires;
D.   A rear view mirror;
E.   A red reflectorized warning device on the front and rear of the non-
highway vehicle;
F.   A slow moving emblem as required by 625 Illinois Compiled Statutes 5/12-
709 attached to the rear of the non-highway vehicle;
G.   A head light that emits white light visible from at least five hundred
feet (500') to the front of the non-highway vehicle;
H.   A tail lamp that emits red light visible from at least one hundred feet
(100') from the rear of the non-highway vehicle;
I.   Brake lights on the rear of the non-highway vehicle; and,
J.   Turn signals on the front and rear of the non-highway vehicle. (Ord. 914-
2018, 9-5-2018)
6-4-5: LIGHTS:
No non-highway vehicle shall be operated on the streets and alleys under the
jurisdiction and control of the Village of Dieterich, Illinois, unless such
non-highway vehicle has its head lights and tail lights illuminated at all
times. (Ord. 914-2018, 9-5-2018)
6-4-6: REQUIRED SEATING; PASSENGERS:
A non-highway vehicle may transport only the number of passengers for which the
specific non-highway vehicle was designed. Every passenger shall sit in a seat
that was installed by the manufacturer of the non-highway vehicle. It shall be
unlawful for the operator/driver of the non-highway vehicle to transport
passengers unless each passenger is in a seat. The operator/driver of the non-
highway vehicle shall not transport anyone who is sitting on the lap of a
passenger, or in any other location except in a seat. (Ord. 914-2018, 9-5-2018)
6-4-7: AGE OF OPERATOR, LICENSE:
No person shall operate a non-highway vehicle on the streets and alleys under
the jurisdiction and control of the Village of Dieterich, Illinois, unless such
operator is at least sixteen (16) years of age and has a valid driver's
license. (Ord. 914-2018, 9-5-2018)
6-4-8: SPEED LIMIT:
No person shall operate a non-highway vehicle on the streets and alleys under
the jurisdiction and control of the Village of Dieterich, Illinois, in excess
of twenty (20) miles per hour. (Ord. 914-2018, 9-5-2018)
6-4-9: ORDINANCE AND VEHICLE CODE OBEYANCE:
During the operation of a non-highway vehicle on any street under the
jurisdiction and control of the Village of Dieterich, Illinois, the operator of
such non-highway vehicle shall obey all applicable rules, regulations, and
ordinances of the Village of Dieterich, Illinois, all applicable provisions of
this Code, and the provisions of the Illinois Vehicle Code, 625 Illinois
Compiled Statutes 5/11-100, et seq., as amended from time to time. (Ord. 914-
2018, 9-5-2018)
6-4-10: VILLAGE LICENSE; ANNUAL FEE:
No Non-Highway Vehicle shall be operated on the streets and alleys under the
jurisdiction and control of the Village of Dieterich, unless said Non-Highway
Vehicle is first licensed by the Village of Dieterich, Illinois. A person
desiring to operate a Non-Highway Vehicle on the streets and alleys under the
jurisdiction and control of the Village of Dieterich, Illinois, shall make
application for a Non-Highway Vehicle license with the Village Clerk of the
Village of Dieterich, Illinois, or his/her designee, on forms provided by the
Village. The license, if issued, shall be valid until December 31 of the same
calendar year of issuance. Thereafter, upon renewal, a license shall be valid
for a period of one year from January 1 in the year of renewal to December 31
of the same calendar year. Prior to the issuance and/or renewal of a Non-
Highway Vehicle license pursuant to this Ordinance, any person applying for a
Non-Highway Vehicle license pursuant to this Ordinance shall pay an annual fee
of $50.00 to the Village Clerk of the Village of Dieterich, Illinois, provided,
however, that if a person applies for an initial license after October 1, the
annual fee shall be reduced to $30.00. Prior to the issuance and/or renewal of
a Non-Highway Vehicle license, an applicant shall also present the Non-Highway
Vehicle to the Village Clerk of the Village of Dieterich, Illinois, or his/her
designee, for an inspection to determine whether the Non-Highway Vehicle
complies with the provisions of this Ordinance and may be operated on the
streets and alleys under the jurisdiction and control of the Village of
Dieterich, Illinois. If the Village Clerk of the Village of Dieterich,
Illinois, or his/her designee determines that the applicant and the Non-Highway
Vehicle comply with the provisions of this Ordinance, then the Village Clerk,
or his/her designee shall issue a license to the applicant. The license shall
be in that form as attached to the ordinance codified herein as Exhibit A and
on file in the Village. (Ord. 990-2019, 11-19-2019)
6-4-11: MANDATORY INSURANCE:
No person shall operate a non-highway vehicle on the streets and alleys under
the jurisdiction and control of the Village of Dieterich, Illinois, unless the
non-highway vehicle is covered by a liability insurance policy as required
under 625 Illinois Compiled Statutes 5/7-601. Every operator of a non-highway
vehicle, shall carry with the non-highway vehicle evidence of insurance as
required by 625 Illinois Compiled Statutes 5/7-602. (Ord. 914-2018, 9-5-2018)
6-4-12: RELEASE OF LIABILITY:
No person shall operate a non-highway vehicle on the streets and alleys under
the jurisdiction and control of the Village of Dieterich, Illinois, unless that
person has executed an Unconditional and Full General Release of Liability,
Waiver, Discharge, and Covenant Not to Sue and filed the same with the Village
Clerk of the Village of Dieterich, Illinois. The Unconditional and Full General
Release of Liability, Waiver, Discharge, and Covenant Not to Sue shall be in
that form as exhibit B on file in the Village. (Ord. 914-2018, 9-5-2018)
6-4-13: LICENSE REVOCATION:
A.   The license issued pursuant to section
6-4-10 of this chapter may be revoked by Village Clerk of the Village of
Dieterich, Illinois, or his/her designee, if:
   1.   There is any material misrepresentation made by the applicant on the
application;
   2.   The liability insurance required by section
6-4-11 of this chapter is no longer in full force and effect;
   3.   There is evidence, as determined in the sole discretion of the Village
Clerk of the Village of Dieterich, Illinois, or his/her designee, that the
permit holder can no longer safely operate the non-highway vehicle; or,
   4.   There has been a violation of any rules, regulations, and ordinances of
the Village of Dieterich, any applicable provisions of this Code, or any
provision of the Illinois Vehicle Code by the license holder.
B.   The Village Clerk of the Village of Dieterich, Illinois, or his/her
designee, shall issue a notice of revocation of a license in writing and either
hand deliver the notice to the permit holder, or send the notice by certified
mail, return receipt required, to the license holder at the address on the
application. The revocation of the license shall be effective immediately after
personal service, or on the third day after the postmark of the certified mail.
In the event of revocation of a license, the license holder shall not be
entitled to the return of any portion of the annual fee. (Ord. 914-2018, 9-5-
2018)
6-4-14: VIOLATIONS; PUNISHMENT:
A.   Any person who violates any provision of this chapter or who aids or abets
the violation of any provision of this chapter shall be guilty of a petty
offense punishable by a fine of not less than one hundred dollars ($100.00) nor
more than seven hundred fifty dollars ($750.00). In addition to any fine, the
Village may seek injunctive and declaratory relief directing the violator(s) to
cure the violation, and the Village may revoke any license authorized and
issued pursuant to this chapter.
B.   A separate offense shall be deemed to be committed on each day during or
on which a violation of any provision of this chapter occurs or continues.
C.   Any second or subsequent offense of any provision of this chapter shall
result in the revocation of the non-highway vehicle license for a period of not
less than three (3) nor more than five (5) years. (Ord. 914-2018, 9-5-2018)
TITLE 7
PUBLIC WAYS AND PROPERTY
CHAPTER 1
STREETS, SIDEWALKS AND PUBLIC WAYS
SECTION:
7-1-1: Supervision
7-1-2: Excavations
7-1-3: Culverts
7-1-4: Encroachments And Obstructions
7-1-5: Moving Buildings
7-1-6: Driving On Streets Under Construction Or Improvement
7-1-7: Use Of Vehicles With Lugs Or Attachments
7-1-8: Prohibited Acts And Conditions
7-1-9: Street Trees
7-1-10: Penalty
7-1-1: SUPERVISION:
The general supervision of the streets, alleys and public sidewalks of the
Village shall be with the person responsible for Village maintenance, under
supervision of the Village Board of Trustees and its Committee on Streets and
Alleys. (1945 Code § 16-1; amd. 2017 Code)
7-1-2: EXCAVATIONS:
A.   It shall be unlawful for any person to make any excavation in any street
or alley without first obtaining a permit from the Village Clerk so to do. The
person obtaining the permit shall then diligently prosecute any necessary work
of excavation and, upon its completion, restore said street or alley to at
least as good a condition as it was prior to such excavation being made, at his
expense.
B.   No person shall wilfully dig up, excavate, or injure or deface any street
or sidewalk upon the streets or alleys of the Village. (1945 Code § 16-7; amd.
2017 Code)
7-1-3: CULVERTS:
A.   Culverts Required: The public health and safety requires that tubes at
ditch crossings at entrances to lots or tracts located within the Village be
installed under the supervision of the Village.
B.   Application For Permit: Lot owners shall make application to the Village
Clerk for permission to install a tube or culvert at driveway entrances to a
lot.
C.   Installation:
   1.   Lot or tract owners shall pay the cost of the tube and the cost of
installing the same.
   2.   Installation of said tube and crossing shall be made under the
direction and supervision of the proper Village officials.
D.   Maintenance By Village: The tube and entrance crossing shall, after
installation, be maintained by the Village. (Ord. 302, 8-3-1970)
7-1-4: ENCROACHMENTS AND OBSTRUCTIONS:
A.   It shall be unlawful for any person to erect or cause to be erected any
building or part thereof within the limits of any public street or alley, or to
fence off or enclose the same, or deny its free and full use to the public. Any
person violating this subsection shall be subject to a fine as provided in
section
7-1-10 of this chapter for each day he shall permit his encroachment on such
street or alley to remain, after receiving notice from any Village officer to
remove the same. (1945 Code § 16-2; amd. 2017 Code)
B.   While a building adjacent to the street or alley is in the course of
construction or repair, tools and materials necessary in such work may be
placed on the adjacent street or alley on obtaining a written permit from the
Village Clerk so to do. But no more than one-third (1/3) of the street or alley
shall be so obstructed, and in no event shall such obstruction be permitted to
remain longer than is necessary for the diligent prosecution of such work, and
if such obstruction is made without a permit or in violation hereof, the
offender shall be subject to a penalty as provided in section
 7-1-10 of this chapter. (1945 Code § 16-5; amd. 2017 Code)
C.   It shall be unlawful for any person to place or leave any obstruction in
any public street which may interfere with its free use by the public. Any
person violating this subsection shall be subject to a fine as provided in
section
7-1-10 of this chapter for each day he permits such obstruction to remain,
after being notified by any Village officer to remove the same. (1945 Code §
16-3; amd. 2017 Code)
7-1-5: MOVING BUILDINGS:
No person shall move or cause to be moved through and upon the streets or
alleys of the Village, any building or structure without first obtaining from
the Village Clerk a permit so to do. No such permit shall be construed to
permit an unreasonable or unnecessary obstruction of the street or alley, nor
be in force for a time longer than is necessary to diligently complete such
moving. (1945 Code § 16-6; amd. 2017 Code)
7-1-6: DRIVING ON STREETS UNDER CONSTRUCTION OR IMPROVEMENT:
No vehicle shall be driven on any street while the same is in process of being
oiled, or when construction or improvement work is in progress thereon, and
when the Village officers have, by appropriate signs or barricades, indicated
the temporary closing of said street to traffic. (1945 Code § 16-11; amd. 2017
Code)
7-1-7: USE OF VEHICLES WITH LUGS OR ATTACHMENTS:
No person shall drive any steam engine, tractor or similar vehicle with lugs or
attachments on the wheel liable to damage the street surface on any paved,
graveled, oiled or hard surfaced streets of the Village, unless said vehicle is
equipped with protective devices to prevent damage to the streets, or unless
the driver planks the street or protects the street from damage. (1945 Code §
16-10; amd. 2017 Code)
7-1-8: PROHIBITED ACTS AND CONDITIONS:
A.   Deposit Of Rubbish Or Trash: It shall be unlawful for any person to throw,
place or deposit any filth, rubbish or trash upon any of the public streets or
alleys of the Village. (1945 Code § 16-4; amd. 2017 Code)
B.   Obstructing Ditches And Drains: It shall be unlawful for any person to
fill up or obstruct or injure or destroy any ditches, sewers or drains of the
Village. (1945 Code § 16-8; amd. 2017 Code)
C.   Riding Or Driving On Sidewalks: It shall be unlawful to ride, drive or
propel any automobiles, motorcycles, side by sides, four-wheelers (except for
snow removal), three- wheelers, golf carts or similar vehicles or conveyances
upon the public sidewalks in the Village. (1945 Code § 16-9; amd. 2017 Code)
7-1-9: STREET TREES:
No person shall plant any tree, bush or shrub on any street or alley, nor cut
or remove any such tree, bush or plant from any public street or alley, without
first obtaining a permit from the Village Clerk so to do. No such permit shall
be issued where such planting would obstruct the usual use of any street, alley
or sidewalk. (1945 Code § 16-16; amd. 2017 Code)
7-1-10: PENALTY:
Any person violating any provisions of this chapter shall be subject to a
penalty of not less than two hundred fifty dollars ($250.00) nor more than
seven hundred fifty dollars ($750.00). (2017 Code)
CHAPTER 2
CONSTRUCTION OF UTILITY FACILITIES WITHIN PUBLIC RIGHTS-OF-WAY
SECTION:
7-2-1: Short Title
7-2-2: Purpose; Intent; Scope; Interpretation
7-2-3: Definitions
7-2-4: Annual Registration Required
7-2-5: Permit Requirements
7-2-6: Insurance; Indemnity; Security
7-2-7: Change In Ownership, Identity Or Legal Status
7-2-8: General Construction Standards
7-2-9: Traffic Control
7-2-10: Location Of Facilities
7-2-11: Construction Methods And Materials
7-2-12: Vegetation Control
7-2-13: Removal, Relocation Or Modifications Of Utility Facilities
7-2-14: Cleanup And Restoration
7-2-15: Maintenance And Repairs
7-2-16: Work To Be Timely
7-2-17: Damage To Water Or Sewer Lines Or Lateral Pipes
7-2-18: Variances
7-2-19: Enforcement And Penalties
7-2-1: SHORT TITLE:
This chapter shall be known, may be cited, and is hereafter designated as the
VILLAGE OF DIETERICH STANDARDS FOR CONSTRUCTION, REPAIR AND MAINTENANCE OF
UTILITY FACILITIES WITHIN PUBLIC WAYS ORDINANCE. (Ord. 775-14, 10-6-2014)
7-2-2: PURPOSE; INTENT; SCOPE; INTERPRETATION:
A.   Purpose: The purpose of this chapter is to establish standards and
procedures for the construction, repair and maintenance of facilities on public
ways within the corporate limits of the Village which shall provide public
benefit consistent with the preservation of the integrity, safe usage and
visual quality of the public ways located within the corporate limits of the
Village.
B.   Intent: By enacting this chapter, the Village intends to exercise its
authority over the public ways within the corporate limits of the Village and
particularly the use of public ways and public property by utility providers by
establishing uniform standards and procedures to address issues presented by
the demand for access to and use of public ways in the Village including, but
not limited to:
   1.   Prevent interference with the use of streets, highways, sidewalks,
