ARTICLE D. R-4 MULTIPLE DWELLING, ATTACHED SINGLE-FAMILY DWELLING AND MOBILE
HOME DISTRICT
SECTION:
10-6D-1: Regulations Established
10-6D-2: Purpose
10-6D-3: Permitted Uses
10-6D-4: Height, Area And Setbacks
10-6D-5: Off Street Parking
10-6D-1: REGULATIONS ESTABLISHED:
The regulations set forth in this article, or set forth in this title when
referred to in this article, are the regulations in the R-4 Multiple Dwelling,
Attached Single- Family Dwelling and Mobile Home District. (Ord. 730-13, 5-6-
2013)
10-6D-2: PURPOSE:
The purpose of the R-4 District is to provide land areas for development of
high density multiple-family dwellings, including apartments, attached single-
family dwellings, and mobile homes, which are areas served by utilities and
well located with respect to public infrastructure. (Ord. 730-13, 5-6-2013)
10-6D-3: PERMITTED USES:
A building or premises shall be used only for the following purposes:
Attached single-family dwelling.
Mobile home.
Multiple-family dwelling.
Nursing or convalescent home.
Accessory building or use customarily incidental to any of the above uses.
(Ord. 730-13, 5-6-2013)
10-6D-4: HEIGHT, AREA AND SETBACKS:
A.   Building Height And Lot Area: The height and area regulations set forth in
chapter 9 of this title shall be observed.
B.   Setbacks: There shall be compliance with the setback requirements set
forth in chapter 9 of this title; provided, however:
   1.   For all attached single-family dwellings, front, rear, and side yard
requirements from exterior building walls to lot lines or to other exterior
building walls shall comply with the requirements of chapter 9 of this title.
   2.   A zero side yard will be permitted in conjunction with a party wall on
an interior lot line used or adopted for joint service between two (2) single
dwelling units.
   3.   The establishment of interior lines bisecting a common wall for
attached single-family dwellings shall be permitted in accordance with the
Village land subdivision ordinance, title 11 of this Code.
   4.   When attached single-family dwellings are attached by common party
walls, each dwelling shall be self-sufficient for all utilities. (Ord. 730-13,
5-6-2013)
10-6D-5: OFF STREET PARKING:
Off street parking space shall be provided in accordance with the requirements
for specific uses set forth in chapter 11 of this title. (Ord. 730-13, 5-6-
2013; amd. 2017 Code)
CHAPTER 7
B-1 GENERAL COMMERCIAL DISTRICT
SECTION:
10-7-1: Regulations Established
10-7-2: Purpose
10-7-3: Permitted Uses
10-7-4: Height, Area And Setbacks
10-7-5: Off Street Parking And Loading
10-7-1: REGULATIONS ESTABLISHED:
The regulations set forth in this chapter, or set forth elsewhere in this title
when referred to in this chapter, are the regulations in the B-1 General
Commercial District. (Ord. 487, 1-7-2002, eff. 2-6-2002)
10-7-2: PURPOSE:
The purpose of the B-1 District is to provide sufficient space in appropriate
locations for retail, office, and commercial activities generally serving a
wide area and located particularly along existing major thoroughfares where a
general mixture of commercial and service activities now exist. (Ord. 487, 1-7-
2002, eff. 2-6-2002)
10-7-3: PERMITTED USES:
A building or premises shall be used only for the following purposes:
   Advertising sign or billboard when located at least fifty feet (50') from
any R District.
   Automobile service establishment.
   Automobile trailer or boat display and sales room.
   Bowling Alley.
   Business or commercial school.
   Dancing or Music Academy.
   Display room for merchandise to be sold at wholesale where merchandise sold
is stored elsewhere.
   Dyeing and cleaning establishment or laundry.
   Farm Implement display and sales room.
   Filling Station.
   Grocery store, frozen food locker.
   Hotel, motel.
   Milk distributing station.
   Motel or tourist home.
   Painting, plumbing or tinsmithing shop.
   Parking or public garage.
   Physician office, medical clinic, veterinarian or animal hospital or riding
academy; provided, that no such building, kennel, or exercise runway shall be
closer than fifty (50') feet to any R District.
   Plant nursery or greenhouse.
   Printing shop.
   Radio or television broadcasting station or studio.
   Restaurant, drive-in restaurant, or other similar place of entertainment or
amusement.
   Sale, leasing or rental of automobiles, trucks, recreational vehicles, boats
or motorcycles, including accessory sale of parts and equipment for, and
accessory service and repair to such vehicles.
   Theatre.
   Tire sales and services, including vulcanizing.
   Upholstering shop, not involving furniture manufacturing.
   Used car sales or storage lot.
   Other general retail, service or repair establishments of similar character
not inconsistent with this chapter.
   Dwellings on any floor above the first floor.
   Accessory building or use customarily incidental to any of the above uses.
All dumpsters, trash receptacles, and other trash service areas shall be
located within the side or rear yard to minimize the effect of their appearance
from any street, freeway, expressway and neighboring property. (Ord. 487, 1-7-
2002, eff. 2-6-2002; amd. Ord. 1134-2023, 5-1-2023)
10-7-4: HEIGHT, AREA AND SETBACKS:
There shall be compliance with the height and area regulations and setback
requirements set forth in chapter 9 of this title. (Ord. 487, 1-7-2002, eff. 2-
6-2002; amd. 2017 Code)
10-7-5: OFF STREET PARKING AND LOADING:
Off street parking and loading spaces shall be provided in accordance with the
requirements for specific uses set forth in chapter 11 of this title. (Ord.
487, 1-7-2002, eff. 2-6-2002; amd. 2017 Code)
CHAPTER 8
M-1 LIGHT INDUSTRIAL DISTRICT
SECTION:
10-8-1: Regulations Established
10-8-2: Purpose
10-8-3: Permitted Uses
10-8-4: Height, Area, And Setbacks
10-8-5: Off Street Parking And Loading
10-8-1: REGULATIONS ESTABLISHED:
The regulations set forth in this chapter, or set forth elsewhere in this title
when referred to in this chapter, are the regulations in the M-1 Light
Industrial District. (Ord. 487, 1-7-2002, eff. 2-6-2002)
10-8-2: PURPOSE:
The purpose of the M-1 District is to provide sufficient space in appropriate
locations for certain types of business and manufacturing, relatively
nonoffensive, in modern buildings with landscaping. (Ord. 487, 1-7-2002, eff.
2-6-2002)
10-8-3: PERMITTED USES:
A building or premises shall be used only for the following purposes:
Any use allowed in the B-1 District.
Generally, those light manufacturing uses similar to those listed below which
do not create any more danger to health and safety in surrounding areas and
which do not create any more offensive noise, vibration, smoke, dust, lint,
odor, heat or glare than that which is generally associated with light
industries of the following specifically permitted types:
A.   Manufacture or assembly of medical and dental equipment, drafting, optical
and musical instruments, watches, clocks, toys, games, and electrical or
electronic apparatus.
B.   Manufacture or assembly of boats, bolts, nuts, screws and rivets,
ornamental iron products, firearms, electrical appliances, tools, dies,
machinery and hardware products, sheet metal products, and vitreous enameled
metal products.
C.   Beverage blending or bottling, bakery products, candy manufacture, dairy
products and ice cream, fruit and vegetable processing and canning.
D.   Manufacture of rugs, mattresses, pillows, quilts, millinery, hosiery,
clothing and fabrics; printing and finishing of textiles and fibers into fabric
goods.
E.   Manufacture of boxes, furniture, cabinets, baskets, and other wood
products of similar nature.
F.   Compounding of cosmetics, toiletries, drugs, and pharmaceutical products.
Accessory uses.
Banks, drive-in or otherwise.
Dwellings for resident watchmen and caretakers employed on the premises.
Offices and office buildings.
Photographic processing or blueprinting.
Printing and publishing.
Railroad right-of-way or spur tracks.
Signs as permitted in the B-1 District.
Wholesale merchandising or storage warehouses. (Ord. 487, 1-7-2002, eff. 2-6-
2002)
10-8-4: HEIGHT, AREA, AND SETBACKS:
The height and area regulations and setback requirements set forth in chapter 9
of this title shall be observed. (Ord. 487, 1-7-2002, eff. 2-6-2002; amd. 2017
Code)
10-8-5: OFF STREET PARKING AND LOADING:
Off street parking and loading spaces shall be provided in accordance with the
requirements for specific uses set forth in chapter 11 of this title. (Ord.
487, 1-7-2002, eff. 2-6-2002; amd. 2017 Code)
CHAPTER 9
HEIGHT AND SETBACK/AREA REQUIREMENTS
SECTION:
10-9-1: Table Of Height And Setback/Area Requirements
10-9-2: Exceptions And Modifications To Requirements
10-9-2-1: Building Height
10-9-2-2: Yards

10-9-2-4: Lot Of Record In Commercial And Industrial Districts
10-9-2-5: Number Of Buildings Per Lot
10-9-3: Access Requirements

lines for each foot of additional height above 45 feet.
(Ord. 684-12, 1-3-2012; amd. Ord. 730-13, 5-6-2013; 2017 Code)
10-9-2: EXCEPTIONS AND MODIFICATIONS TO REQUIREMENTS:
10-9-2-1: BUILDING HEIGHT:
A.   The height regulations prescribed herein shall not apply to television and
radio towers, wireless communications facilities, church spires, belfries,
monuments, tanks, water and fire towers, stage towers or scenery lofts, cooling
towers, ornamental towers and spires, chimneys, elevator bulkheads,
smokestacks, conveyors and flagpoles. (Ord. 705-12, 6-4-2012)
B.   Public, semipublic or public service buildings, hospitals, institutions or
schools, where permitted, may be erected to a height not exceeding sixty feet
(60'), and churches and temples may be erected to a height not exceeding
seventy five feet (75') when the required front, side and rear yards are each
increased by one foot (1') for each foot of additional building height above
the height regulations for the district in which the building is located.
C.   The limitation on number of stories shall not apply to buildings used
exclusively for storage purposes, provided such buildings do not exceed the
height in feet permitted in the district in which they are located. (Ord. 487,
1-7-2002, eff. 2-6-2002)
10-9-2-2: YARDS:
A.   Front Yards:
   1.   When fifty percent (50%) or more of the frontage on one (1) side of the
street between two (2) intersecting streets is improved with buildings that
have a front yard which is greater or less than the required front yard in the
district, no building shall project beyond the average front yard so
established; provided, however, that a front yard depth shall not be required
to exceed fifty percent (50%) in excess of the front yard otherwise required in
the district in which the lot is located.
   2.   On lots having double frontage, the required front yard shall be
provided on both streets.
   3.   No fence, sign, structure, or planting higher than thirty inches (30")
above the established street grades shall be maintained within twenty feet
(20') of any street intersection right-of-way.
   4.   An open, uncovered porch or paved terrace may project into a required
front yard for a distance of not more than ten feet (10'), but this shall not
be interpreted to include fixed canopies.
   5.   Filling station pumps and pump islands and signs may be located within
a required yard, provided they are not less than fifteen feet (15') from any
street line and not less than fifty feet (50') from the boundary of any
residential district.
B.   Side Yards:
   1.   On a corner lot, the width of the yard along the side street shall not
be less than any required front yard on such street; provided, however, that
the buildable width of a lot of record shall not be reduced to less than thirty
five feet (35').
   2.   No accessory building shall project beyond the required yard line along
any street.
   3.   Where dwelling units are erected above a commercial establishment, no
side yard is required except when required for the commercial building on the
side of a lot adjoining a residence district.
   4.   Where a lot of record on July 1, 2002, is less than fifty one feet
(51') in width, each of the required side yards may be reduced by an amount
equal to ten percent (10%) of the difference between such width and fifty one
feet (51'); provided, however, that no side yard shall be less than three feet
(3').
C.   Rear Yards:
   1.   Where a lot abuts upon an alley, one-half (1/2) the alley width may be
considered as part of the required rear yard.
   2.   No accessory buildings shall be closer than ten feet (10') to the main
building unless it is attached to or forms a part of such main structure, nor
closer than six feet (6') to a rear lot line or three feet (3') to any side lot
line.
   3.   The ordinary projections of sills, belt courses, cornices and
ornamental features may extend to a distance not to exceed eighteen inches
(18") into a required yard. Roofs and eaves may extend not more than thirty
inches (30") into a required yard.
   4.   Open or lattice enclosed fire escapes and the ordinary projections of
chimneys and flues into a rear yard may be permitted by the Village Board for a
distance not to exceed five feet (5') when these are so placed as not to
obstruct light and ventilation. (Ord. 487, 1-7-2002, eff. 2-6-2002)
10-9-2-3: LOT AREA PER FAMILY:
Where a lot of record on July 1, 2002, has less area or width than herein
required in the district in which it is located and the owner of such lot does
not own any other parcel or tract adjacent thereto, said lot may nonetheless be
used for a one-family dwelling or for any nondwelling use permitted in the
district in which it is located. (Ord. 487, 1-7-2002, eff. 2-6-2002)
10-9-2-4: LOT OF RECORD IN COMMERCIAL AND INDUSTRIAL DISTRICTS:
Where a lot of record exists on July 1, 2002, in a commercial or industrial
district prohibiting residences, such lot of record may be used for
construction of a single-family dwelling and must meet the yard requirements in
the applicable R District. (Ord. 487, 1-7-2002, eff. 2-6-2002)
10-9-2-5: NUMBER OF BUILDINGS PER LOT:
There may be two (2) or more related multi-family, commercial, industrial or
institutional buildings on a lot; provided, that the required yards are
maintained around the group of buildings. (Ord. 487, 1-7-2002, eff. 2-6-2002)
10-9-3: ACCESS REQUIREMENTS:
A.   Access to a use located on a collector or major thoroughfare as designated
in the Comprehensive Plan shall not have more than one (1) 24-foot wide
entrance to said thoroughfare for the parcel on which said use is located;
except, that a parcel having more than two hundred feet (200') of frontage on
said thoroughfare may have an additional twenty four foot (24') wide entrance.
B.   Any new entrance to a public street shall require an access permit in
accordance with Village standards.
C.   For all uses in the B-1 and M-1 Districts, there shall be provided a
clearly marked fire/emergency lane, not less than twelve feet (12') in width,
adjacent to all pedestrian doors and parking areas, plainly marked so as to
prohibit parking thereon or obstruction thereof in any way. (Ord. 487, 1-7-
2002, eff. 2-6-2002)
CHAPTER 10
SIGNS
SECTION:
10-10-1: Maximum Height And Area
10-10-2: Signs In And Adjacent To R Districts
10-10-1: MAXIMUM HEIGHT AND AREA:
No sign shall have a height of more than thirty feet (30'). No sign shall be
larger than one hundred fifty (150) square feet in area. (Ord. 487, 1-7-2002,
eff. 2-6-2002)
10-10-2: SIGNS IN AND ADJACENT TO R DISTRICTS:
A.   Portable Signs: There shall be no portable signs placed on any lot in any
R district for a period longer than ten (10) days in any thirty (30) day
period. There shall be no portable signs placed in any lot in any A1, B, or M-
1 District for a period longer than thirty (30) days in any sixty (60) day
period. (Ord. 487, 1-7-2002, eff. 2-6-2002; amd. 2017 Code)
B.   Illuminated Signs:
   1.   No sign shall be illuminated in any R district.
   2.   No sign on any lot that is adjacent to any R district shall be
illuminated unless the illumination plan for such sign is approved by the Board
of Zoning Appeals and Planning. The illumination of the sign shall not
unreasonably interfere with the quiet enjoyment of the property in the R
district. (Ord. 487, 1-7-2002, eff. 2-6-2002)
CHAPTER 11
OFF STREET PARKING AND LOADING
SECTION:
10-11-1: Parking Spaces On Same Lot; Exceptions
10-11-2: Parking Requirements For Certain Districts
10-11-3: Number Of Parking Spaces
10-11-4: Number Of Loading Spaces
10-11-1: PARKING SPACES ON SAME LOT; EXCEPTIONS:
A.   All parking spaces required herein shall be located on the same lot with
the building or use served; except, that where an increase in the number of
spaces is required by a change or enlargement of use, or where such spaces are
provided collectively or used jointly by two (2) or more buildings or
establishments, the required spaces may be located not to exceed three hundred
feet (300') from a residential building served and not to exceed five hundred
feet (500') from any nonresidential building served.
B.   In any case where the required parking spaces are not located on the same
lot with the building or use served, or where such spaces are collectively or
jointly provided and used, a written agreement to assure their retention for
such purposes shall be properly drawn and executed by the parties concerned,
approved as to form by the Village. (Ord. 684-12, 1-3-2012)
10-11-2: PARKING REQUIREMENTS FOR CERTAIN DISTRICTS:
Parking in the indicated districts shall be in accordance with the following
requirements:
A.   B And M Districts: Off street parking facilities and the required parking
facilities in any B or M District may be located in the front yard but shall
not be nearer than twenty feet (20') to an R-1 or R-2 District.
B.   R Districts:
   1.   Driveways and surfaced parking areas shall not occupy more than fifty
percent (50%) of the front yard of any parcel in an R District except for
parcels occupied by multiple dwellings.
   2.   In a residential district, no recreational vehicle or trailer may park
other than on private property and shall not cause a visibility obstruction at
the intersection of street rights-of-way. No vehicle or trailer shall be used
as a dwelling while parked on private property.
   3.   Trucks and trailers in excess of twelve thousand (12,000) pounds
designed and manufactured for or used for specific commercial purposes
including, but not limited to, wreckers, dump trucks, tracked vehicles, buses,
construction vehicles, equipment carriers, bottling works delivery trucks,
grain trucks and refrigerated trucks are prohibited from parking in an R
District. No vehicle in excess of twelve thousand (12,000) pounds gross vehicle
weight, excluding recreational trailers and recreational vehicles, shall be
parked in an R District.
   4.   Inoperable or unlicensed passenger vehicles and trailers shall be
parked within an enclosed structure in an R District. (Ord. 684-12, 1-3-2012)
   5.   Not more than five (5) licensed vehicles, including allowed
recreational vehicles and trailers, shall be permanently parked on a parcel of
property in an R-1, R-2, R-3 or R-4 District. (Ord. 730-13, 5-6-2013)
C.   Exceptions: Any type commercial vehicle, regardless of gross vehicle
weight, delivering or picking up merchandise for delivery or employed in
performing a repair or construction service may park for the purpose of making
such pick up or delivery or for the duration of the period during which a
repair or construction service is being performed on or to property in the area
where parked. (Ord. 684-12, 1-3-2012)
10-11-3: NUMBER OF PARKING SPACES:
A.   Enumerated: In all districts, there shall be provided at the time any
building or structure is erected or structurally altered (except as specified
in subsections B and C of this section) minimum off street parking spaces in
accordance with the following requirements:

B.   Computation Of Number Of Spaces: In computing the number of such parking
spaces required, this shall be construed to be the nearest whole number; and in
the case of mixed uses, the parking spaces required shall equal the sum of the
requirements of the various uses computed separately.
C.   Increase In Number Of Spaces Required:
   1.   Whenever a building or use constructed or established after the
effective date hereof is changed or enlarged in floor area, number of
employees, number of dwelling units, seating capacity or otherwise to create a
need for an increase of ten percent (10%) or more in the number of existing
parking spaces, such spaces shall be provided on the basis of the enlargement
or change.
   2.   Whenever a building or use existing prior to the effective date hereof
is enlarged to the extent of fifty percent (50%) or more in floor area or in
the area used, said building or use shall then and thereafter comply with the
parking requirements set forth herein. (Ord. 684-12, 1-3-2012)
10-11-4: NUMBER OF LOADING SPACES:
Every building or part thereof erected or occupied for retail business,
service, manufacturing, storage, warehousing, hotel, mortuary or any other use
similarly involving the receipt or distribution by vehicles of materials or
merchandise shall provide and maintain on the same premises one loading space
for every ten thousand (10,000) square feet or fraction thereof of floor area
in the building. (Ord. 684-12, 1-3-2012)
CHAPTER 12
SOLAR ENERGY SYSTEMS REGULATIONS
SECTION:
10-12-1: Short Title
10-12-2: Purpose
10-12-3: Solar Energy System - General Regulations
10-12-1: SHORT TITLE:
   This Chapter shall be known and may be sited as the Dieterich Solar Energy
Systems Regulations.
(Ord. 1158-2024, 4-1-2024)
10-12-2: PURPOSE:
   The purpose of this Chapter 12 is to establish reasonable and uniform
regulations for the location, installation, operation and maintenance of Solar
Energy Systems; to assure that any development and production of Solar Energy
Systems is safe and to minimize any potentially adverse effects on the
community; to promote the supply of sustainable and renewable energy resources,
in support of national, state and local goals; and to facilitate energy cost
savings and economic opportunities for residents and businesses situated within
the corporate limits and or extraterritorial jurisdiction of the Village of
Dieterich, Illinois. (Ord. 1158-2024, 4-1-2024)
10-12-3: SOLAR ENERGY SYSTEM - GENERAL REGULATIONS:
   Solar Energy Systems may be erected or installed on properties within the
corporate limits of the Village of Dieterich, Illinois, in accordance with this
Chapter, as well as all State and Federal laws and regulations, as amended from
time to time, concerning the use and operation of said Solar Energy System, and
shall be further subject to the following standards:
   A.   Except as authorized by the Board of Trustees for public utility and/or
public infrastructure purposes and except for Ground Mounted Solar Energy
Systems granted a special use permit under Section 10-3B-1, Solar Energy
Systems shall only be permitted if accessory to a principal building and/or
principal use.
   B.   Any person seeking to erect, construct, install, or maintain an
interconnected Solar Energy System on property located within the corporate
limits of the Village of Dieterich, Illinois, shall submit an application to
the Village Clerk prior to the installation of any Solar Energy System. As part
of the application, a person seeking to erect, construct, install, or maintain
an interconnected Solar Energy System shall also submit a written narrative
and/or graphic form, which includes all of the items below: 
      1.   Name, address, and telephone number of property owner;
      2.   Name, address, and telephone number of the installer of the Solar
Energy System;
      3.   Description of the proposed Solar Energy System indicating the
following:
         a.   Plan showing the proposed location of the Solar Energy System;
         b.   System dimensions and specifications;
         c.   Evidence showing compliance with all applicable setback
requirements;
         d.   Evidence showing compliance with applicable setback and/or height
regulations;
         e.   Distance to any roads or overhead utility lines; and,
         f.   Compliance with each regulation contained in this Chapter 12.
         g.   All Solar Arrays with building mounted inverters or arrays with
inverters mounted on the array within ten (10) feet of a structure, shall
comply with NEC 2020 rapid shut down requirements.
      4.   The permit application shall be supplemented by any specifications,
plans, or other information considered pertinent in the judgment of the Village
Clerk; and,
      5.   An application shall be accompanied by a Twenty Dollar ($20.00)
application fee, which shall be deposited with the Village Clerk.
   C.   Solar Energy Systems shall be installed according to manufacturer
specifications and in accordance with all applicable building codes, electrical
codes, fire codes, and other ordinances, codes, rules, and regulations
pertaining to Small Solar Energy Systems.
   D.   Electric solar energy system components must have a UL listing.
   E.   Solar Energy Systems shall have a lockable, utility accessible, load
breaking, manual disconnect switch, which can be utilized to connect and/or
disconnect all electric solar energy system components. The manual disconnect
switch shall be located not more than four (4) feet from the building’s
electric service meter. The manual disconnect switch shall not be obstructed
from access in any manner, including, but not limited to, landscaping, shrubs,
trees, terraces, fencing, etc.
   F.   All Solar Energy Systems shall have the following caution labels
installed and/or placed on said Solar Energy System:
      1.   A “Caution Solar Electric System” label shall be installed and/or
placed adjacent to the manual disconnect switch;
      2.   “Caution Solar Circuit” directional labels shall be placed on any
and all DC raceways and equipment and shall depict the direction of the
electrical flow inside said raceway and/or other equipment. Said “Caution Solar
Circuit” directional labels shall be located and spaced out not more than every
ten (10) feet along said raceway; and,
      3.   All caution labels shall be weather resistant and reflective, with a
red background and white lettering with a minimum of 3/8 inch lettering.
   G.   Reflection angles from Solar Collector Surfaces shall be oriented away
from residential buildings.
   H.   Type Permitted and Maximum Roof Area:
      1.   Flush Mounted Solar Energy Systems (6" or less) are permitted to be
installed on any roof area;
      2.   Non-Flush Mounted Solar Energy Systems are permitted on a building
with a flat roof if the Solar Collector Surface is completely screened from
view to an observer five (5) feet above the ground at any point along an
abutting property line;
      3.   Non-Flush Mounted Solar Energy Systems are prohibited on any roof
that is adjacent to the front yard and/or corner side yard;
      4.   The Solar Collector Surface area shall be set back on the roof as
follows:
         a.    Set back from the roof lower eves shall be no lower than six (6)
inches from the shingle line;
         b.   Set back from the roof top edge (ridge) a minimum of two (2)
feet;
         c.   Solar panels shall not extend past the roof edge on sides; and,
         d.   Set back from any roof equipment and/or other obstructions
(examples: chimneys, exhaust fans, vents, etc.) a minimum of one (1) foot,
except skylights shall have a minimum of two (2) feet;
   I.   Maximum Permitted Height & Building Projection/Extension:
      1.   The Solar Energy System shall conform to the height regulations of
the zoning district in which the property where the Solar Energy System is to
be installed, mounted, built is located;
      2.   Non-Flush Mounted Solar Energy Systems shall not extend above the
highest point on the roof line; and,
      3.   Solar Energy Systems shall not project/extend beyond the exterior
wall of any building on which said Solar Energy System has been installed,
mounted, or built.
   J.   Ground Mounted Solar Energy Systems. Ground Mounted Solar Energy
Systems shall be prohibited in the Village of Dieterich, Illinois, except by
the applicant securing a special use permit variance in accordance with Section
10-3B-1 of this Title 10.
   K.   Abandoned Systems. Any Solar Energy System that is inactive or
inoperable for a period of twelve (12) continuous months shall be deemed
abandoned. If the Solar Energy System is deemed abandoned, the owner is
required to repair or remove the Solar Energy System from the property at the
owner’s expense within ninety (90) days after notice from the Village.
(Ord. 1158-2024, 4-1-2024)
TITLE 11
SUBDIVISION REGULATIONS
CHAPTER 1
GENERAL SUBDIVISION PROVISIONS
SECTION:
11-1-1: Purpose
11-1-2: Extra-Territorial Jurisdiction
11-1-3: Definitions
11-1-4: Variances
11-1-5: Amendments
11-1-6: Appendices Adopted
11-1-7: Validity
11-1-8: Enforcement
11-1-9: Violation; Penalty
11-1-1: PURPOSE:
This title is hereby enacted to provide for the health, comfort, safety and
convenience of the inhabitants of the Village and vicinity; to establish
reasonable standards of design for subdivisions and for resubdivision of
improved land and of areas subject for public service facilities, parks,
playgrounds, and other public grounds; to provide that no map or plat of a
subdivision within the corporate limits, as designated by the Village Board of
Trustees, shall be recorded unless it provides for streets, alleys and public
grounds in conformity with the adopted official plan for the Village. (Ord.
488, 1-7-2002, eff. 2-6-2002)
11-1-2: EXTRA-TERRITORIAL JURISDICTION:
The Village Board of Trustees hereby elects not to exercise its extra-
territorial jurisdiction over that territory located within one and one-half
(11/2) miles from its corporate boundaries; provided, however, that the Village
Board of Trustees reserves its right to reconsider the exercise of the extra-
territorial jurisdiction, in accordance with applicable Illinois law and notice
provisions, at a later date. (Ord. 488, 1-7-2002, eff. 2-6-2002)
11-1-3: DEFINITIONS:
For the purpose of this title, certain terms and words are defined as follows:
   ALLEY: A public right-of-way designed to serve as a secondary access to the
side or rear of those properties whose principal frontage is on a street.
   AREA:
Area, Gross: The entire area within the boundary lines of the property proposed
for subdivision/development, including any areas to be dedicated/reserved for
street and alley rights-of-way and for public uses.
Area, Net: The entire area within the boundary lines of the tract proposed for
subdivision, less the area to be dedicated for street and alley rights-of-way
and/or other public purposes.
   BLOCK: A tract of land bounded by streets or by a combination of streets,
public parks, cemeteries, railroad rights-of-way, waterways or boundary lines
of the corporate limits of the Village.
   BOARD: Village Board of the Village of Dieterich.
   COMPREHENSIVE PLAN: The plan or any portion thereof adopted by the Village
of Dieterich for the coordinate physical development of Dieterich and environs.
   DRIVEWAY: Private accessway leading from a street or alley to a dwelling
unit or building.
   EASEMENT: A strip of land upon which the owner grants a right of use to
another for one (1) or more designated purposes.
   FLAG LOT: A lot fronting on or abutting a public road and where access to
the public road is by narrow, private right- of-way.
   FRONTAGE: The dimensions of a lot measured at the street right-of-way.
   IMPROVEMENT: Street work and utilities including, but not limited to, water,
sewer, electric, gas and storm drainage, to be installed or agreed to be
installed by the subdivider on land to be used for streets and/or easements, as
are necessary for the general use of lot owners in the subdivision, local
neighborhood traffic and drainage needs as a condition precedent to the
approval and acceptance of the final plat thereof.
   LOT: A portion of a subdivision or other parcel of land established for
transfer of ownership or for building development, whether immediate or future.
   LOT WIDTH: The lesser of the width of a lot at the front building line or
back building line.
   OWNER: Any person, firm, association, syndicate, partnership, corporation,
trust, or any other legal entity having sufficient proprietary interest in the
land sought to be subdivided to commence and maintain proceedings to subdivide
the same under this title.
   PARCEL: Any existing area of land under single ownership which may be
transferred according to applicable laws and ordinances without further
surveying or platting being required.
   PLANS: All drawings, including general plans, cross sections, profiles,
working details and specifications, which the subdivider prepares or has
prepared to show the character, extent and details of the improvements required
in chapter 5 of this title.
   PLAT: A map or drawing showing the lot and street arrangement or other
features or details of the area being subdivided as required in this title for
preliminary and final approval and recording.
   SETBACK LINE: A line that is roughly parallel to the front, side or rear lot
line establishing the minimum space to be provided as the front, side or rear
yard.
   STREET: A public or private thoroughfare which affords the principal means
of access to abutting properties and whether designated as a freeway,
expressway, thoroughfare, highway, road, parkway, avenue, boulevard, lane,
place, circle, or however otherwise designated.
   STREET, COLLECTOR: A street designated as a collector on the adopted Major
Streets Plan of the Village or a street in a proposed subdivision which is
intended to collect traffic from the minor streets within a neighborhood or a
portion thereof and to distribute such traffic to arterial thoroughfares, in
addition to providing access to properties abutting thereon.
   STREET, CUL-DE-SAC: A minor street having but one (1) end open for vehicular
traffic and with the other end permanently terminated by a circular turnaround.
   STREET, DEAD END: A street having only one (1) end open to vehicular
traffic; also referred to as a court.
   STREET, LOCAL OR MINOR: A street other than an arterial thoroughfare or
collector street and intended primarily for providing low volume traffic access
to abutting properties of limited number.
   STREET, MAJOR: A collector street or State or Federal highway.
   STREET, STUB: A street that is temporarily terminated with a T-turnaround
but is planned for future continuation.
   STREET, TURNAROUND: A temporary arrangement as shown in the Subdivision
Standards to provide a means for vehicles to turn around at the end of a stub
street.
   STREET, URBAN RESIDENTIAL NONCOLLECTOR: A local street in an area zoned
single-family residential.
   SUBDIVIDE: The process of dealing with land so as to establish a subdivision
as defined in this section.
   SUBDIVIDER: Any person, firm, association, syndicate, partnership,
corporation, trust, or any other legal entity, dividing or proposing to divide
land so as to constitute a subdivision as defined in this section and including
any agent of the subdivider.
   SUBDIVISION:
   A.   Either: 1) the division of land into two (2) or more parcels, any of
which is less than five (5) acres, except for a subdivision defined herein as a
minor subdivision; or 2) the establishment or dedication of land for all or a
portion of a road, highway, street, or alley upon a tract of land regardless of
size.
   B.   For purposes of this title, the following shall be considered a minor
subdivision; provided, that, such minor subdivision does not create lots or
parcels which conflict with the zoning regulations, as contained in title 10 of
this Code, the land subdivision regulations, as contained in this title, the
Village of Dieterich Comprehensive Plan, or the Official Map of the Village of
Dieterich:
      1.   The revision of lot width or lot depth in an approved subdivision
where all affected lots are under single ownership and which will not involve
any streets or easements of access or drainage and utility easements; or
      2.   The sale or exchange of a parcel of land, or any portion thereof,
between owners of adjoining and contiguous land, except where the transfer
results in the creation of another buildable lot.
   C.   For purposes of this title, the following shall not be considered a
subdivision:
      1.   The conveyance of parcels of land or interest therein for use as
right-of-way for railroads or other public utility facilities and other
pipelines which does not involve any new streets or easements of access;
      2.   Conveyances relating to the dedication of land for public use or
instruments relating to the vacation of land impressed with a public use; or
      3.   A conveyance made to correct a description in a prior conveyance.
   VILLAGE BOARD OF ZONING APPEALS AND PLANNING: Village of Dieterich Board of
Zoning Appeals and Planning.
   ZERO SIDE YARD LOT: A lot located in an R-3 or R-4 District of the Village
zoned for attached single-family housing (duplex). (Ord. 488, 1-7-2002, eff. 2-
6-2002; amd. Ord. 683-12, 1-3-2012; 2017 Code)
11-1-4: VARIANCES:
Whenever the tract to be subdivided is of such unusual size or shape or is
surrounded by such development or unusual conditions that the strict
application of the requirements contained in this title would result in real
difficulties or substantial hardship or injustice, the Board, after report by
the Board of Zoning Appeals and Planning, may vary or modify such requirements
so that the subdivider may develop his property in a reasonable manner, but so
that at the same time, the public welfare and interests of the Village and
surrounding area are protected and the general intent and spirit of this title
preserved. (Ord. 488, 1-7-2002, eff. 2-6-2002)
11-1-5: AMENDMENTS:
Any regulations or provisions of this title may be changed and amended from
time to time by the Village Board; provided, however, that such changes or
amendments shall not become effective until after study and report by the
Village Board of Zoning Appeals and Planning and until after a public hearing
has been held, public notice of which shall have been given in a newspaper of
general circulation at least fifteen (15) days prior to such hearing. (Ord.
488, 1-7-2002, eff. 2-6-2002)
11-1-6: APPENDICES ADOPTED:
The appendices on file in the Village are hereby adopted and incorporated by
this reference as though fully stated herein. (Ord. 488, 1-7-2002, eff. 2-6-
2002)
11-1-7: VALIDITY:
If any section, subsection, sentence, clause or phrase of this title is, for
any reason, held to be unconstitutional or void, such decision shall not affect
the validity of the remaining portions of this title. (Ord. 488, 1-7-2002, eff.
2-6-2002)
11-1-8: ENFORCEMENT:
It shall be the responsibility of the Village to enforce the provisions of this
title. (Ord. 488, 1-7-2002, eff. 2-6-2002; amd. 2017 Code)
11-1-9: VIOLATION; PENALTY:
It shall be illegal to sell any lot, tract or property which does not conform
to the requirements and regulations of this title, and every such sale or
attempt to sell shall be subject to a fine of not less than seven hundred fifty
dollars ($750.00) for each lot or tract. (Ord. 488, 1-7-2002, eff. 2-6-2002;
amd. 2017 Code)
CHAPTER 2
PLATTING PROCEDURES GENERALLY
SECTION:
11-2-1: Plats Required
11-2-2: Preapplication Conference
11-2-3: Minor Subdivisions
11-2-4: Preliminary Plat
11-2-5: Final Plat
11-2-6: Recording Plats
11-2-7: Transfer Of Land; Access Permits
11-2-1: PLATS REQUIRED:
The owner, agent or person having control of any land within the corporate
limits of the Village who proposes to divide land into two (2) or more parcels,
any one (1) of which is less than five (5) acres, shall be required to
subdivide such land into lots, blocks, streets, avenues, alleys, public ways,
and grounds by a plat in accordance with the laws of the State of Illinois and
the provisions of this title. (Ord. 488, 1-7-2002, eff. 2-6-2002)
11-2-2: PREAPPLICATION CONFERENCE:
The subdivider shall meet with the Village Engineer (or his designee) prior to
submitting the preliminary plat. The purpose of this meeting is to discuss the
subdivision regulations and the procedure, criteria and standards contained
therein; and to familiarize the subdivider with the Village Comprehensive Plan
and proposals of the Plan affecting the area in which the subdivision lies.
(Ord. 488, 1-7-2002, eff. 2-6-2002)
11-2-3: MINOR SUBDIVISIONS:
Any person proposing to subdivide land as defined as a minor subdivision in
section
11-1-3 of this title, definition of subdivision, shall submit to the Village
Engineer a final plan prepared in accordance with the specifications of chapter
6 of this title. The design and layout of the subdivision shall conform to the
requirements of chapter 3 of this title. The Village Engineer shall submit the
plat of the minor subdivision to the Village Board for its consideration and
approval or disapproval. (Ord. 488, 1-7-2002, eff. 2-6-2002)
11-2-4: PRELIMINARY PLAT:
A.   Any person proposing to subdivide land, other than a minor subdivision,
shall submit to the Village Board of Zoning Appeals and Planning, through the
Village Engineer, for its consideration, a preliminary plat prepared in
accordance with the specifications of chapter 4 of this title. The design and
layout of the subdivision shall conform to the requirements of chapter 3 of
this title. Following consideration of the preliminary plat, the Board of
Zoning Appeals and Planning shall report its findings and recommendations in
writing to the Board for its consideration and approval or disapproval.
B.   If requested by the person offering the proposed preliminary plat, the
Village Engineer may permit such person to prepare a final plat for submission
to the Board at the same time the preliminary plat is submitted. (Ord. 488, 1-
7-2002, eff. 2-6-2002)
11-2-5: FINAL PLAT:
A.   When Submitted Concurrently With Preliminary Plat: Following the
recommendation for approval of the preliminary plat by the Board of Zoning
Appeals and Planning, the subdivider shall: 1) install the required
improvements (at his own risk); or 2) arrange to furnish a bond, letter of
credit, or similar security for such installation, all in accordance with the
requirements of chapter 5 of this title. Upon approval of the improvements, or
arrangements therefor, the final plat shall be submitted to the Village Board
in accordance with the provisions and requirements of chapter 6 of this title.
B.   When Preliminary Plat Has Had Prior Board Approval: Following approval of
the preliminary plat by the Board of Zoning Appeals and Planning and the Board,
the subdivider shall: 1) install the required improvements; or 2) arrange to
furnish a bond, letter of credit, or other security for such installation, all
in accordance with the requirements of chapter 5 of this title. Upon approval
of the improvements, or arrangements therefor, the final plat shall be
submitted to the Village Board in accordance with the provisions and
requirements of chapter 6 of this title. (Ord. 488, 1-7-2002, eff. 2-6-2002)
11-2-6: RECORDING PLATS:
No subdivision plat, as defined in this title, shall be filed for record or
recorded in the Office of the County Recorder of Deeds unless and until the
approval of the Board is endorsed thereon by the Village Clerk and unless and
until the property being subdivided conforms to the Village zoning regulations.
(Ord. 488, 1-7-2002, eff. 2-6-2002)
11-2-7: TRANSFER OF LAND; ACCESS PERMITS:
No parcel of land in a subdivision created after April 4, 1961, shall be
transferred, sold, or offered for sale; nor shall an access permit be issued
for any structure thereon; nor shall a certificate of occupancy for the use of
any land or structure thereon be issued until a plat of subdivision shall have
been recorded with the County Recorder of Deeds in accordance with this title.
Any person who violates this section shall be subject to the penalties
contained herein. (Ord. 488, 1-7-2002, eff. 2-6-2002)
CHAPTER 3
DESIGN STANDARDS
SECTION:
11-3-1: Existing Topography
11-3-2: Streets And Alleys
11-3-3: Easements
11-3-4: Blocks
11-3-5: Lots
11-3-6: Maintenance Of Improvements Outside Corporate Limits
11-3-7: Engineer Review
11-3-1: EXISTING TOPOGRAPHY:
The arrangement of streets and lots shall give due regard to the topography and
other physical features of the property. (Ord. 488, 1-7-2002, eff. 2-6-2002)
11-3-2: STREETS AND ALLEYS:
A.   Relation To Adjoining Street System:
   1.   The arrangement of streets in new subdivisions shall make provision for
the continuation of the existing streets in adjoining areas (or their proper
projection where adjoining land is not subdivided) insofar as they may be
deemed necessary for public requirements.
   2.   The street and alley arrangements shall not be such as to cause
hardship to owners of adjoining property in platting their own land and
providing convenient access to it.
   3.   Offset streets shall be avoided where possible.
   4.   The angle of intersection between minor streets and major streets shall
not vary by more than ten degrees (10°) from a right angle. Streets obviously
in alignment with existing streets shall bear the names of the existing
streets.
   5.   Proposed street names that are in conflict with existing street names
shall not be approved. (Ord. 488, 1-7-2002, eff. 2-6-2002)
B.   Minimum Street Widths:
   1.   Right-of-way width for streets shall be a minimum of fifty feet (50')
for urban residential, non-collector streets and fifty feet (50') for all other
streets.
   2.   Pavement surface width shall be a minimum of twenty four feet (24')
from edge to edge of pavement (exclusive of curb and gutter width) for urban
residential, non-collector streets, and a minimum of twenty four feet (24')
from edge to edge of pavement (exclusive of curb and gutter width) for all
other streets.
C.   Alleys:
   1.   Alleys shall not be provided in a residential block.
   2.   Alleys are required at the rear of all business lots, unless other
adequate provisions are made for services and deliveries, and shall be at least
twenty feet (20') wide. (Ord. 875-18, 2-5-2018)
D.   Private Streets: There shall be no private streets platted in any
subdivision. (Ord. 488, 1-7-2002, eff. 2-6-2002)
11-3-3: EASEMENTS:
A.   Easements of at least ten feet (10') in width shall be dedicated on each
side of lot lines and street rights-of-way, where necessary, for Village
utilities and storm sewers. Easements of greater width may be required along or
across lots where necessary for the extension of main sewers or where both
water and sewer lines are located in the same easements. Additional easements
for other utilities shall be provided as necessary.
B.   Whenever any stream or surface drainage course is located in an area being
subdivided, the subdivider shall provide an adequate easement along each side
of the stream for the purpose of widening, deepening, sloping, improving or
protecting the stream, and such easement shall be dedicated to the Village or
other appropriate public agency. (Ord. 488, 1-7-2002, eff. 2-6-2002)
11-3-4: BLOCKS:
A.   No residential block shall be longer than one thousand two hundred feet
(1,200'). Where blocks are over seven hundred fifty feet (750') in length, a
crosswalk with a right-of-way of at least ten feet (10') in width may be
required near the center of the block. (Ord. 488, 1-7-2002, eff. 2-6-2002)
B.   Courts, dead end streets, or other street space may be provided if proper
access is given to all lots from a dedicated street or court. (Ord. 488, 1-7-
2002, eff. 2-6-2002; amd. 2017 Code)
11-3-5: LOTS:
A.   The lot arrangement and design shall be such that all lots will provide
satisfactory and desirable building sites, properly related to topography and
to the character of surrounding development.
B.   All side lines of lots shall be at right angles to straight street lines
and radial to curved street lines except where a variation of this rule will
provide a better street and lot layout. Lots with double frontage shall be
prohibited in residentially zoned areas.
C.   No lot other than a zero side yard lot shall have a depth of less than one
hundred feet (100') or a depth in excess of three (3) times its width. No lot
shall have an area or width less than that required by the zoning ordinance.
D.   Lots at street intersections shall have a radius of twenty feet (20') at
the street corner, except a chord may be required in lieu of the circular arc
where warranted.
E.   Corner lots shall have a width sufficient to permit the establishment of
front building lines on both sides of the adjoining streets.
F.   All lots shall front on a public street. The frontage of a lot shall be
not less than eighty percent (80%) of the width of a lot at the front setback
line.
G.   Flag lots shall be prohibited. (Ord. 488, 1-7-2002, eff. 2-6-2002)
11-3-6: MAINTENANCE OF IMPROVEMENTS OUTSIDE CORPORATE LIMITS:
Where a subdivision outside the corporate limits contains sewers, sewage
treatment plants, water supply systems, park areas or other physical facilities
necessary or desirable for the welfare of the area and of common use or benefit
which the Village, Township, County or park district does not desire to
maintain, provision shall be made by trust agreements, deed restrictions or
other arrangements acceptable to the Village, for the proper and continuous
maintenance and supervision of such facilities by the lot owners in the
subdivision. (Ord. 488, 1-7-2002, eff. 2-6-2002)
11-3-7: ENGINEER REVIEW:
The standards set forth herein shall be considered minimum standards, and the
Village Engineer, upon concurrence of the Board, may increase or modify the
standards contained herein where, in the exercise of reasonable engineering
judgment and based upon the impact of the subdivision upon the public, the
circumstances require such increase or modification. (Ord. 488, 1-7-2002, eff.
2-6-2002)
CHAPTER 4
PRELIMINARY PLAT
SECTION:
11-4-1: Filing Preliminary Plat; Fees
11-4-2: Required Information
11-4-3: Approval Of Plat
11-4-1: FILING PRELIMINARY PLAT; FEES:
Six (6) copies of the preliminary plat, drawn to scale of not more than one
hundred feet to an inch (1" = 100'), shall be submitted to the Village Board of
Zoning Appeals and Planning through the Village Engineer. The plat shall be
accompanied by payment of a filing fee of one hundred fifty dollars ($150.00)
or the sum of five dollars ($5.00) for each lot within the proposed
subdivision, whichever is greater, and a nonrefundable two hundred fifty dollar
($250.00) engineering review fee. In the event the engineering review cost to
the Village exceeds the two hundred fifty dollar ($250.00) engineering review
fee, the Village shall notify the person submitting the plat in advance, and
such person shall be responsible for such additional engineering review cost,
or such person may withdraw the plat. (Ord. 488, 1-7-2002, eff. 2-6-2002)
11-4-2: REQUIRED INFORMATION:
A.   The preliminary plat shall show:
   1.   The location of the present property lines and section lines and
streets, buildings, watercourses and other existing features within the area to
be subdivided and similar information regarding land immediately adjacent
thereto.
   2.   The proposed location and width of streets, alleys, lots and easements.
   3.   Existing sanitary and storm sewers, water mains, culverts and other
underground structures within the tract and immediately abutting thereto; the
location and size of the nearest water main and sewer outlet.
   4.   The title under which the proposed subdivision is to be recorded and
the name of the professional engineer, the registered land surveyor and the
subdivider platting the tract.
   5.   Contours referred to the Village datum with intervals of five feet (5')
or less.
   6.   The north point, scale and date.
   7.   Floodplain boundaries as shown on the Federal Emergency Management
Agency Flood Hazard Map.
   8.   Engineer's and owner's certificates related to topographical and
profile studies pertaining to surface drainage as required by 765 Illinois
Compiled Statutes 205/2. The engineer shall provide a copy of the drainage
study to the Village Engineer.
   9.   Plans or written statements describing the grades or profiles of the
streets, the proposed grades and facilities for all required improvements and
the subdivider's proposal to the Village for accomplishing their installation
in accordance with chapter 5 of this title.
   10.   The location of all setback lines.
B.   The preliminary plat shall have on its face a statement identifying any
aspects of the plat not in conformance with this title. (Ord. 488, 1-7-2002,
eff. 2-6-2002)
11-4-3: APPROVAL OF PLAT:
A.   If the Board of Zoning Appeals and Planning finds that the preliminary
plat satisfies the requirements of this title, it shall recommend approval by
the Board. If the Board of Zoning Appeals and Planning finds otherwise, it
shall specify in writing objections found to such plat and may either recommend
disapproval or recommend approval conditioned upon specific changes in the
plat.
B.   One (1) copy of the proposed plat, together with a copy of the findings of
the Board of Zoning Appeals and Planning, shall be submitted to the Board; one
(1) copy of the proposed plat and findings shall be retained by the Board of
Zoning Appeals and Planning; one (1) copy of the proposed plat and findings of
the Board of Zoning Appeals and Planning and the Board, if applicable, shall be
given to the person offering the proposed plat. (Ord. 488, 1-7-2002, eff. 2-6-
2002)
CHAPTER 5
REQUIRED IMPROVEMENTS
SECTION:
11-5-1: Plans And Specifications
11-5-2: Installation Of Improvements
11-5-3: Survey Monuments
11-5-4: Public Ways
11-5-5: Water Facilities
11-5-6: Sewer Facilities
11-5-7: Drainage
11-5-1: PLANS AND SPECIFICATIONS:
A.   Preliminary Plans And Specifications:
   1.   The subdivider shall submit preliminary plans and specifications to the
Village Engineer for required improvements in compliance with applicable
policies and standards of the Village.
   2.   The Village Engineer shall review the preliminary plans and
specifications for minimum improvements and report these findings to the
subdivider.
   3.   If the Village Engineer shall find such preliminary plans and
specifications to be in accordance with applicable policies and standards of
the Village, he shall determine the amount of bond, letter of credit or other
security, if required.
   4.   Following the approval of the plans and specifications by the Village
Engineer, the subdivider may submit his final plat to the Village Clerk for
approval.
B.   Final Plans And Specifications: The final plans and specifications for
minimum improvements shall include the following:
   1.   Additional details required by the Village Engineer;
   2.   Appropriate permit applications required by other governmental
agencies;
   3.   Supporting engineering calculations as required by the Village
Engineer; and
   4.   Proposed construction schedule;
and shall be filed with the Village Engineer before construction commences,
unless a later date is approved by the Village Engineer. (Ord. 488, 1-7-2002,
eff. 2-6-2002)
11-5-2: INSTALLATION OF IMPROVEMENTS:
A.   Before Final Plat Approval Or Security In Lieu Thereof:
   1.   No final plat of any subdivision shall be approved unless: a) the
improvements listed in this chapter have been installed prior to such approval;
or b) the subdivider shall have arranged to file with the Village a performance
bond, letter of credit or other security to ensure the construction of the
improvements listed in this chapter in a satisfactory manner and within the
period specified by the Board, such period not to exceed twelve (12) months. No
performance bond, letter of credit or other security shall be accepted unless
it is enforceable by or payable to the Village in a sum at least equal to the
cost of construction of the improvements as estimated by the Village Engineer
and in a form and with security approved by the Village Board. All such
performance bonds, letters of credit or other security shall be secured with
deposits of cash, commercial surety company, bank letters of credit or other
similar guarantees approved by the Village Counsel.
   2.   The Village shall inspect the construction to assure compliance with
the approved plans and specifications. The cost of such inspection shall be
paid by the person submitting the plat. The Village Board may allow inspection
to be provided by the design engineer whose seal appears on the plans and
specifications for improvements in lieu of inspection by the Village. No
improvements shall be accepted unless inspected pursuant to this title and
found by the Village Board to meet the requirements of this title.
   3.   Should the period of time set by the Village lapse without completion
and acceptance of the improvements and without an extension of time being
granted, the Village shall take necessary steps to proceed with the
accomplishment and completion of the improvements, making use of the security
on the bond, letter of credit or other security.
   4.   For all subdivisions, a set of as built plans for all subdivision
improvements shall be filed in the Village Engineer's Office by the subdivider
upon completion of said improvements. The as built plans should have a
statement attached and signed and sealed by a registered engineer that the
improvements are correctly shown on the as built plans and conform to the
approved specifications. Such signature shall appear on all separate sheets
comprising the as built plans and specifications.
   5.   When the Village Engineer has ascertained that all the improvements
have been completed, that said improvements conform to the standards and
requirements of the Village, and a set of as built plans has been filed, the
Village shall accept the improvements by resolution and shall return all unused
security deposited by the subdivider.
B.   Part Of Improvements: The owner of a tract may prepare and secure approval
of a preliminary plat for the entire tract and may install the required
improvements only in a portion of such tract, but the improvements must be
installed or provision made for the installation in any portion of the area for
which a final plat is approved for recording; provided, however, that any water
mains, storm sewers, trunk sewers, and sewage treatment plants shall be
designed and built to serve the entire tract or designed and built in such a
manner that they can easily be expanded or extended to serve the entire tract.
(Ord. 488, 1-7-2002, eff. 2-6-2002)
11-5-3: SURVEY MONUMENTS:
All subdivision boundary corners shall be marked with survey monuments set
flush with the ground or other surface, two (2) of which shall be permanent
monuments. A permanent monument shall be deemed to be concrete with rod center
at least thirty inches (30") long with a minimum width of three inches (3").
Should conditions prohibit the placing of monuments on the line, off-set
monuments will be permitted; provided, however, that such monuments shall be
identified on the subdivision plat in relation to the true lines or corners.
Iron pipes or steel rods at least thirty inches (30") in length shall be set
flush with the ground at all lot corners. If survey monuments are removed
during construction, they shall be replaced by a registered land surveyor
before the final plat is approved and/or before improvements are accepted by
the Village. All subdivisions must be referenced to two (2) United States
Public Land Survey Corners of Record, and all monuments must conform to 765
Illinois Compiled Statutes 205/1. (Ord. 488, 1-7-2002, eff. 2-6-2002)
11-5-4: PUBLIC WAYS:
All streets, curbs and gutters, sidewalks and public ways shall be installed in
accordance with standards and specifications as established by the Village
Board. (Ord. 488, 1-7-2002, eff. 2-6-2002)
11-5-5: WATER FACILITIES:
A.   Each lot within a subdivision shall be provided with a connection to the
Village water system.
B.   Fire hydrants shall also be installed in all subdivisions, and the
location of the same shall be approved by the fire official.
C.   The water supply system shall be constructed under the direction and
control of, and all construction shall be subject to the approval of, the
Village and shall conform to Illinois Environmental Protection Agency rules,
regulations and standards. (Ord. 488, 1-7-2002, eff. 2-6-2002; amd. 2017 Code)
11-5-6: SEWER FACILITIES:
Each lot within a subdivision shall be provided with a connection to a sanitary
sewer, said sewer connection to terminate not less than two feet (2') inside
the curb line or easement line. All connections to the Village sewer system and
the subdivision sewer system shall comply with the ordinance of the Village
pertaining to sewers, and all construction of the system shall be subject to
the direction and approval of the Village Engineer. (Ord. 488, 1-7-2002, eff.
2-6-2002; amd. 2017 Code)
11-5-7: DRAINAGE:
The plat shall be laid out to provide proper drainage of the area being
subdivided, including facilities such as curbs and gutters, catch basins,
culverts, bridges and natural waterways. The design of the storm drainage
system shall be according to accepted engineering practices and Village
standards and specifications as established by the Village Board. (Ord. 488, 1-
7-2002, eff. 2-6-2002)
CHAPTER 6
FINAL PLAT
SECTION:
11-6-1: Description
11-6-2: Submission Of Final Plat; Recommendations
11-6-3: Required Information
11-6-4: Village Board Approval; Recording Final Plat
11-6-1: DESCRIPTION:
The final plat shall be drawn on tracing cloth, film acetate, or similar
permanent material at a scale of not more than one hundred feet to the inch (1"
= 100') from an accurate survey and on one (1) or more sheets where maximum
dimensions shall not exceed seventeen inches by twenty two inches (17" x 22").
If more than two (2) sheets are required, an index sheet of the same dimensions
shall be filed showing the entire subdivision on one (1) sheet and the
component areas shown on the other sheets. (Ord. 488, 1-7-2002, eff. 2-6-2002)
11-6-2: SUBMISSION OF FINAL PLAT; RECOMMENDATIONS:
The original and ten (10) prints of the final plat shall be submitted to the
Village Board of Zoning Appeals and Planning through the Village Clerk at least
one (1) week before the meeting thereon. When the final plat conforms to the
approved preliminary plat, if any, and the requirements of this chapter and
chapter 5 of this title have been accomplished, certification to this effect
shall be endorsed on the final plat by the Chair of the Board of Zoning Appeals
and Planning or evidenced by separate written certification from the Chair of
the Board of Zoning Appeals and Planning and the plat thereupon submitted to
the Board for its approval or disapproval. Where the final plat does not
conform to the approved preliminary plat, the Board of Zoning Appeals and
Planning shall submit its recommendations to the Board for approval or
disapproval of the final plat. (Ord. 488, 1-7-2002, eff. 2-6-2002)
11-6-3: REQUIRED INFORMATION:
The final plat and accompanying documents shall show:
A.   The boundary lines of the area being subdivided with accurate distances
and angles. The correct legal description of the property being subdivided
shall be shown on the plat.
B.   The lines of all proposed streets and alleys with their widths and the
names of all streets.
C.   An accurate outline of any portions of the property intended to be
dedicated or granted for public use.
D.   Floodplain boundaries as determined by the flood hazard maps of the
Federal Emergency Management Agency.
E.   The lines of all adjoining properties and the limits of adjoining streets
and alleys with their widths, and names of all streets.
F.   All lot lines and an identification of all lots and blocks.
G.   The location of all easements provided for public use, services or
utilities.
H.   All dimensions, both linear and angular, necessary for locating the
boundaries of the subdivision, lots, streets, alleys, easements and other areas
for public or private use. Linear dimensions are to be given to the nearest 1/
100th of a foot.
I.   The radii, arcs or chords, points of tangency and central angles for all
curvilinear streets and radii for rounded corners.
J.   The location of all survey monuments and their descriptions.
K.   The gross area, net area and lot area of the land being subdivided.
L.   The name of the subdivision and the scale of the plat, points of the
compass, and the name of the owner or owners or subdividers.
M.   A certificate signed and dated by the owner, appearing on the plat and on
all separate sheets comprising the plat acknowledging the private restrictions
spelled out on the plat. Should these restrictions or trusteeships be of such
length as to make their lettering on the plat impracticable and thus
necessitate the preparation of separate instrument, reference to such
instrument shall be made on the plat.
N.   A certificate of platting signed and dated by the owner, appearing on or
attached to the plat and on all separate sheets comprising the plat,
acknowledging the dedication to public use of all streets, alleys, parks or
other open spaces shown thereon and the granting of easements required. (Ord.
488, 1-7-2002, eff. 2-6-2002)
O.   A certificate signed and dated by the owner and the Village Clerk stating
that there are no unpaid taxes or assessments upon any part of the area within
the subdivision. (Ord. 488, 1-7-2002, eff. 2-6-2002; amd. 2017 Code)
P.   A certificate signed, dated and sealed by a registered Illinois land
surveyor, attesting to the accuracy of the survey and the correct location of
all monuments shown on the plat.
Q.   A certificate signed and dated by a registered Illinois land surveyor
that:
   1.   The subdivision is or is not in a floodplain. (Ord. 488, 1-7-2002, eff.
2-6-2002)
   2.   The subdivision is or is not within the incorporated Village limits.
(Ord. 488, 1-7-2002, eff. 2-6-2002; amd. 2017 Code)
R.   A certificate for those subdivisions that border the water of the State of
Illinois to be approved by the Illinois Department of Transportation.
S.   A certificate for those subdivisions that front on a street maintained by
the Illinois Department of Transportation. (Ord. 488, 1-7-2002, eff. 2-6-2002)
11-6-4: VILLAGE BOARD APPROVAL; RECORDING FINAL PLAT:
After the approval of the final plat by the Village Board, said plat shall be
recorded in the County Recorder's Office. Within ninety (90) days of approval,
if not so recorded, such plat shall have no validity and shall not be recorded
without reapproval. (Ord. 488, 1-7-2002, eff. 2-6-2002)
